وعند الشَّافِعِي له لا يحل بيع المطعومات حفنة بحفنتين بناء على ما ذكرنا من العلة، وبناءً على أن الأصل عندنا الحل، وعنده الحرمة، فعندنا ما يدخلُ في الكيل يثبت فيه الحرمة ، وما لا يدخلُ فيه يَبْقَى على أصله، وهو الحل، وعند الشَّافِعِي الأصل هو الحرمة، والمساواة مخلص فيما لا يَدْخُلُ في المسوى الشرعي، وهو الكيلُ يبقى على الأصل، وهو الحرمة ، وإنما جعل الحرمة أصلاً ؛ لقوله : لا تبيعوا الطَّعامَ بالطَّعام إلا سواء بسواء فما لا يكون مساوياً كان حراماً. قلنا : المعنى لا تبيعوا الطعام الذي يدخلُ في المسوى الشرعي إلا سواء بسواء والحاصل أنَّ ما لا يدخل تحت المعيار إما لقلة كالحفنة والحفنتين، والتمرة والتمرتين، وإما لكونه عددياً لا يباع بالمعيار الشرعي كالبيضة والبيضتين، والجوزة والجوزتين يحل البيع متفاضلاً ؛ لعدم جريان القدر والمعيار، فلا يوجد المساواة، فلم يتميّز الفضلُ وبقي على الأصل، وهو الحل عندنا. خلافاً للشافعي له ؛ لوجودِ علة الحرمة وهي الطَّعم مع عدم المخلص، وهو المساواة، فيحرم، لأن الأصل عنده الحرمة والحفنة دومشت از طعام وجزآن، ومنه يقال : نحن حفنة من حفنات الله تعالى ؛ أي يسير بالإضافة إلى رحمته وملكه، كذا في «الصراح»، وفي «النهاية»: الحفنة : ملء الكف. [1] قوله : وإنما ...الخ ؛ حاصله : إنَّ الشافعي له إنما جعل الحرمة أصلاً ؛ لأنه : «نهى عن بيع الطعام بالطعام ، واستثنى منه ما يكون مساوياً، فعلم أن بيع الطعام بالطعام منهي عنه وحرام إلا ما يكون بالتساوي، فما لا يكون مساوياً يبقى حرام. (۳) [٢] قوله : قلنا...الخ ؛ حاصله : إنَّ المراد من الطعام في قوله : «لا تبيعوا...الخ» ليس مطلقاً، وأعم من أن يكون قليلاً أو كثيراً ، بل الطعام الذي يدخل تحت المعيار الشرعي، فما نحن فيه خارج عن هذا القول، وهذا كما يقال : لا تقتل الحيوان إلا بالسكين. فليس المراد في هذه المقولة مطلقاً، وأعم من أن يصلح الحيوان مقتولاً بالسكين أو لا حتى يشمل القمل والبرغوث ونحوهما، بل المراد ما يمكن قتله بالسكين، فكذا هاهنا ، وفيه مباحث تركناها ؛ لغرابة المقامِ وطوالة الكلام. (۱) قوله : أي إن وجد.... الخ ؛ توضيحه أنه لما ثبت أنَّ العلة شيئان، فلا يخلو : ١ . إما أن يوجدا معاً. ٢. أو يفقدا معاً. ٣. أو وجد أحدهما دون الآخر.
And according to al-Shafi'i, it is not permissible to sell foodstuffs a handful for two handfuls based on what we mentioned of the cause, and based on that the default with us is permissibility, and with him is prohibition. So with us, what enters into the measure (kayl) has prohibition established for it, and what does not enter into it remains on its original ruling, which is permissibility. And with al-Shafi'i, the default is prohibition, and equality is a deliverance; what does not enter into the legal equalizer, which is measurement, remains on the default, which is prohibition. He only made prohibition the default because of his statement: 'Do not sell food for food except like for like.' So whatever is not equal is prohibited. We say: The meaning is: Do not sell food that enters into the legal equalizer except like for like. The gist is that what does not fall under the standard, either due to small quantity like a handful or two handfuls, or a date or two dates, or because it is countable not sold by legal standard like an egg or two eggs, or a walnut or two walnuts, then selling is permissible with disparity; because capacity and standard do not apply, so equality does not exist, and the excess is not distinguished and remains on the default, which is permissibility with us. Contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the cause of prohibition exists, which is edibility, with no deliverance, which is equality, so it is prohibited, because the default with him is prohibition. And the handful is ... of food and two parts, from which it is said: We are a handful of handfuls of Allah Almighty, meaning insignificant in addition to His mercy and dominion. Like in al-Sirah, and in al-Nihayah: al-hafnah: filling the palm. [1] His statement: 'And only... etc.'; its gist: Al-Shafi'i only made prohibition the default because he (peace be upon him) forbade selling food for food and excepted from it what is equal, so it is known that selling food for food is prohibited and forbidden except what is equal, so what is not equal remains prohibited. (3) [2] His statement: 'We said... etc.'; its gist: The meaning of food in his statement 'Do not sell...' is not absolute and general, whether little or much, but rather food that falls under the legal standard. So what we are discussing is outside this saying. This is like when it is said: Do not kill animals except with a knife. The meaning in this statement is not absolute and general including whether the animal can be killed with a knife or not to include lice and fleas and the like, but rather the meaning is what can be killed with a knife. So similarly here. And there are investigations we have left due to the strangeness of the context and length of speech. (1) His statement: 'That is if found... etc.'; its clarification: When it is established that the cause is two things, then it is not free: 1. Either both exist together. 2. Or both are absent together. 3. Or one exists without the other.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the ruling on selling food items in unequal quantities when the measure (kayl) does not apply. The author first states the Shafi'i position: it is not permissible to sell a handful of food for two handfuls, because the cause ('illa) of prohibition (edibility and measure) exists, and the default with Shafi'i is prohibition. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the default is permissibility (ibaha), and only food that enters into legal measurement (kayl or wazn) triggers prohibition. Small quantities like a handful or countable items like eggs are not subject to standard measurement, so the original permissibility remains. The author then explains the Shafi'i proof from the hadith 'Do not sell food for food except like for like' and how the Hanafis interpret 'food' restrictively to mean food that is customarily measured. An analogy is given: the command 'Do not kill animals except with a knife' does not apply to lice or fleas, which cannot be killed with a knife. Similarly, the hadith about food only applies to food that can be measured. The passage ends with an outline of the conditions for the cause of riba: when both capacity/jins (genus) are present, both excess and delay are prohibited; when both are absent, both are permitted; when one is present, excess is permitted but delay is not. This clarifies the Hanafi position that the 'illa for riba is twofold: measure and genus. The passage is a typical expansion_probe, where the commentator (the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah) explains and expands upon the rulings from the base text (likely al-Wiqayah or its sharh).

Key Terms
الحفنة (al-hafnah): The amount that fills the palm of the hand; a handful. Used as an example of a small quantity that is not measured by standard legal measures (kayl).
المسوى الشرعي (al-musawwi al-shar'i): The legal equalizer; that which establishes equality in quantity, such as measurement by kayl (volume) or wazn (weight). Items not subject to this equalizer are not required to be equal in riba transactions.
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause or legal reason for the prohibition of riba. In this context, it is twofold: genus (jins) and measure (kayl or wazn). Both must be present for riba to apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible to sell one handful of wheat for two handfuls of wheat hand-to-hand?
A) No, because it is riba al-fadl.
B) Yes, because handfuls are not measured by legal standards.
C) Yes, but only if the wheat is of different quality.
D) No, because the hadith prohibits selling food for food except like for like.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits selling food in unequal small quantities when standard measures are not used, based on the absence of the 'illa of measurement and the default of permissibility.

Riba Rulings Based on Genus and Quantity
Explaining the Hanafi 'illa for riba as genus and quantity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi 'illa of genus and quantity to determine the ruling of riba al-fadl and riba al-nasiah in various exchange transactions.

Core Idea
Riba is prohibited only when both genus and quantity meet; partial cause triggers credit prohibition.

In this lesson, we delve into the Hanafi doctrine of riba, examining the dual attributes (al-wasfan) that constitute the effective cause. By analyzing when both, one, or neither attribute is present, you will learn to distinguish permissible exchanges from prohibited ones. The key insight is that a partial cause (shubha) is enough to forbid credit even when excess is allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Determine whether both attributes (genus and quantity) are present, both absent, or only one present in the exchange.
Genus refers to the type of commodity; quantity refers to weight or volume measure.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For each scenario, state whether riba al-fadl (excess) and riba al-nasiah (credit) are haram or halal.
When both present: both fadl and nasiah haram. Both absent: both halal. One present: fadl halal, nasiah haram.
3
Understand the role of shubha
Explain why a single attribute (e.g., quantity alone) still prohibits credit. Reason: it creates a semblance (shubha) of the complete cause, and shubha in riba is treated like reality regarding credit.
Credit is prohibited because it involves selling a non-existent countervalue (ma'dum).
4
Apply the examples
Work through the examples given: wheat for barley (different genus, same quantity) and Harawi cloth for Harawi cloth (same genus, different quantity). Verify the rulings.
In wheat for barley hand to hand, fadl halal but nasiah haram. In cloth case, same.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
Note that the Shafi'i school defines the 'illa as genus and edibility, leading to different applications (e.g., salt is edible, so riba applies; cloth is not).
This distinction explains why the cloth example is debated.

Or one is present without the other. So in credit, one of the two counter-values is non-existent, and selling a non-existent thing is not permissible, so this meaning becomes a preponderant factor for that semblance, so it is not permissible; and in non-credit, the semblance is not considered because we said that semblance is inferior to reality; moreover, the well-known hadith (1) [1] 1. If both are present, excess is prohibited: as when selling a measure of wheat for two measures of it, and credit is also prohibited even if equal, as when selling a measure of wheat for a measure of it on credit, and its verification is as before. 2. And if both are absent, excess and credit are permissible: as when selling a Harawi cloth for two Marwani cloths on credit, this sale is permissible due to the absence of the cause; for the absence of the cause, even if it does not necessitate a ruling, yet when the cause is unified, its absence leads to absence [of ruling], not in the sense that it causes absence, but rather existence is not established due to its absence, so the absence of ruling, which is lack of prohibition in our case, remains on its original state; and when the cause of prohibition is absent, and the original principle in sales is permissibility except what evidence excludes, what is established is permissibility. Thus in 'al-Fath'. 3. And if one is present without the other, as when selling wheat for barley, or selling a Harawi cloth for a Harawi cloth, excess is permissible and credit is prohibited; because the conjunction of quantity and genus is the reality of the cause, so one of them has a semblance of the cause; thus, by the reality of the cause, actual excess is prohibited (which is due to quantity because it is real excess), and by the semblance of the cause, a semblance of excess is prohibited (which is credit) because it resembles excess but is not actual excess, applying the evidence to the extent possible. It cannot be said: one [attribute] is part of the cause, and by it the ruling is not established, so how can the prohibition of credit be established by one of them? For we say: one of them is a complete cause for this ruling, which is the prohibition of credit, even if it is part of the cause with respect to riba al-fadl in reality, so there is no necessary objection. Thus in the gloss of al-Durr al-Mukhtar by 'Allama al-Tahtawi quoting from al-Halabi. (1) His statement: moreover, the well-known hadith; its apparent meaning indicates that it is a reasoning for both issues, but this hadith agrees with the case when selling a measure of wheat for two measures of barley hand to hand, but in the case of Harawi cloth it does not; (1) Fath al-Qadir (6:153). (2) Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar (3:108).
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rulings of riba, specifically when the two attributes (al-wasfan) of genus (jins) and quantity (qadr) are present or absent in exchange transactions. The author, following the Hanafi school, identifies the effective cause (illa) for riba as a combination of genus and quantity (measured by weight or volume). The passage explains three scenarios:

1. **Both attributes present** (e.g., exchanging wheat for wheat of different measures or on credit): Both riba al-fadl (excess) and riba al-nasia (credit/deferred payment) are prohibited. This is the full application of the 'illa.

2. **Both attributes absent** (e.g., exchanging a Harawi cloth for two Marwani cloths on credit): The sale is permissible because the cause of riba is completely absent. The default in sales is permissibility unless evidence indicates otherwise.

3. **One attribute present, the other absent** (e.g., wheat for barley hand to hand, or five cubits of Harawi cloth for six cubits hand to hand): In this case, excess (fadl) is permissible because the 'illa is not fully realized, but credit (nasiah) is prohibited. The author explains that even a partial cause creates a semblance (shubha) of riba, and in the case of credit, this semblance is treated like reality because credit involves selling a non-existent countervalue (ma'dum). The example of not killing animals except with a knife is used to illustrate that the ruling applies only when the condition can be met.

The passage then cites authorities: 'al-Fath' (Fath al-Qadir) and 'Hashiyat al-Durr al-Mukhtar' by al-Tahtawi. The commentary concludes with a note that the well-known hadith supports the case of wheat/barley but not the cloth case, indicating that riba in cloth is not based on hadith directly but on qiyas (analogy). The overriding principle is that shubha is considered in prohibition but to a lesser degree than certainty.

Overall, this is a masterful Hanafi exposition of riba's 'illa, demonstrating how the school balances textual evidence and rational analogy.

Key Terms
الفضل (al-fadl): Excess in quantity of one countervalue over the other in a ribawi transaction.
النساء (al-nasī'ah): Deferred payment or credit in a sale, even if the quantities are equal.
الجنس (al-jins): Genus or type of commodity; e.g., all types of wheat are same genus, but wheat and barley are different genera.
القدر (al-qadr): Quantity measured by weight or volume; e.g., a measure (qafiz) of grain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person sells one measure of wheat for two measures of barley hand to hand, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school based on the passage?
A) Both fadl and nasiah are haram.
B) Only fadl is haram.
C) Only nasiah is haram.
D) Both are halal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits credit when even one attribute of the 'illa is present due to the semblance of riba, even if excess is allowed.

The Semblance of Riba: Does One Attribute Prohibit Deferred Exchange?
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on whether same type alone prohibits riba al-nasi'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that a single ribawi attribute (e.g., same type) creates a semblance (shubha) sufficient to invalidate a deferred sale, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view requiring both attributes.

Core Idea
A semblance of riba (shubha) has the same legal effect as actual riba in prohibiting the transaction.

In Islamic commercial law, the prohibition of riba aims to prevent exploitation in exchanges. But does a mere resemblance to riba trigger the same prohibition? This lesson addresses a critical disagreement between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i: when a single attribute of a ribawi commodity—such as the same type (jins) or same measure (kayl/wazn)—is present, is a deferred (nasi'a) exchange already prohibited? The Hanafi argument relies on the concept of shubha (semblance) as an effective legal impediment. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how causes (ʻillal) and their semblances operate in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a sale of the same type of ribawi commodity (e.g., a Herawi garment for another Herawi garment) on credit is invalid (fasid) due to the semblance of riba. Note that the Hanafi school considers the presence of a single attribute (same type) sufficient to create shubha.
The hukm level is fasid, not batil, because the defect is the semblance of riba, not its reality.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one attribute alone does not prohibit nasa' ; both type and measure must be present for the prohibition to apply. For him, selling a Herawi garment on credit is valid if the types differ (e.g., garment for money).
The Shafi'i position is based on the idea that the prohibition of riba al-nasi'a requires both attributes to be present.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i dalil: the reality of riba (fadl) is not established with one attribute; only a semblance (shubha) exists, and a semblance should not be an impediment. They cite that selling a garment for two on credit is permitted when types differ, so a mere semblance is even less restrictive.
The opposing argument relies on the principle that only actual riba (not its semblance) invalidates a contract.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: each attribute (type alone or measure alone) has a 'shubhat al-illiyya' (semblance of causation). Just as the reality of the cause (haqiqat al-illa) establishes actual riba, its semblance establishes a semblance of riba. And shubha blocks permissibility like the reality does. Therefore, the sale is invalid to avoid the possibility of riba.
The key principle: 'al-shubhatu mani'atun 'an al-jawaz ka al-haqiqah' (the semblance prevents permissibility like the reality).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: For Hanafis, selling a Herawi garment for two on credit is invalid; for Shafi'is, it is valid as long as the types differ (e.g., garment for money). This shows the legal consequence of accepting or rejecting shubha as a valid impediment.
This disagreement affects many transactions involving ribawi commodities.

(۲)
وعند الشَّافِعِي (٢) له الجنس بانفرادِهِ لا يُحَرِّمُ النَّس ) .
لاتحادِ الجنس فيه، فافهم.
[١]قوله : الجنس بانفراده ؛ قال في «النهاية» : ليس للتّخصيص فائدة ؛ فإنه كذلك الكيلُ والوزن، وحاصله : أن وجود أحدِ وصفي الربا لا يحرِّمُ النَّسَاء عنده ، فهو ينكر حرمة النساء. [٢] قوله : لا يُحرم النساء ؛ لأنَّ بالنقديَّةِ وعدمها لا يثبت إلا شبهة الفضل ، وحقيقة الفضل غير مانع فيه ؛ أي في الجنسين يجوز بيع الثوب الهروي الواحد بالاثنين ، فالشبهة أولى أن لا يكون مانعاً. ولنا : أنه مال الربا من وجه نظراً إلى القدر وحده ، كما في الحنطة مع الشعير، أو الجنس وحده كالثوب الهروي مع الثوب الهروي، والنقدية أوجبت فضلاً في المالية فتحقق شبهة الربا في محل صالح لعلة صالحة لها.
والشبهة مانعة عن الجواز كالحقيقة حتى فسد البيع مجازفة ؛ لاحتمال الربا ؛ وهذا لأن كل حكم تعلّق بوصفين مؤثرين لا يتم نصاب العلة إلا بهما ، فلكل واحدٍ منهما شبهة العلية، فيثبت بشبهة العليَّةِ شبهه الفضل، كما يثبت بحقيقتها حقيقته، هذا ما لخصته. من «الهداية» (۳) و«الكفاية»(4) ، وغيرهما.
And it is his statement: 'When the two types differ, then sell as you wish as long as it is hand-to-hand' supports what we said. (2) According to al-Shafi'i (2), the type alone does not prohibit nasi'a because of the unity of type there, so understand. [1] His statement: the type alone; he said in al-Nihaya: There is no benefit to specification, for it is the same with measure and weight. The summary is that the existence of one of the two attributes of riba does not prohibit nasi'a in his view, so he denies the prohibition of nasi'a. [2] His statement: does not prohibit nasi'a, because through monetary property and its absence, only the semblance of surplus (shubha al-fadl) is established, and the reality of surplus is not an impediment there; meaning in two types, selling one Herawi garment for two is permitted, so the semblance (shubha) is even more deserving of not being an impediment. To us (Hanafis): it is property subject to riba from one perspective, considering only the quantity, like wheat with barley, or the type alone like a Herawi garment with a Herawi garment, and monetary property necessitates a surplus in value, so a semblance of riba is realized in a place fit for an effective cause fit for it. And the semblance (shubha) prevents permissibility like the reality, to the extent that the sale is invalid if it involves uncertainty (mujazafa), due to the possibility of riba. And this is because every ruling attached to two effective attributes only completes the requirement of the cause through both, so each one has a semblance of causation (shubha al-illiyya), and through the semblance of causation, the semblance of surplus is established, just as through its reality the reality of surplus is established. This is what I summarized from al-Hidayah, al-Kifayah, and others.

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The issue is whether the presence of a single attribute of riba (either same type or same measure/weight) alone is sufficient to prohibit riba al-nasi'a (deferred exchange). The Shafi'i view is that only when both attributes (type and measure/weight) are present does prohibition apply. The Hanafi argument is that each attribute separately creates a semblance (shubha) of riba, and a semblance suffices to invalidate the transaction, analogously to the reality of riba. The author supports this with logical reasoning and references to earlier Hanafi works like al-Hidayah and al-Kifayah. The practical difference is that for the Hanafis, selling one Herawi garment for two on credit would be invalid due to the semblance of riba from same type, whereas for the Shafi'is it would be permissible as long as the type differs. The Hanafi position is that the sale is corrupt (fasid) due to the possibility of riba.

Key Terms
النَّسَاء (al-nasa'): Deferred payment or credit sale; specifically riba al-nasi'a is the riba that arises from deferment in exchange of ribawi items.
شُبْهَة (shubha): A semblance or doubt; here it refers to the semblance of riba that suffices to invalidate a transaction, even if the actual riba is not confirmed.

B) Because the presence of same type creates a semblance of riba, which prohibits
C) Because it is not hand-to-hand
D) Because the Shafi'i school forbids it

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a semblance of riba (shubha) is sufficient to invalidate a deferred exchange when a single ribawi attribute is present, even if actual riba is not established.

The Six Commodities Are Always Measured or Weighed
Ruling that six named ribawi items are always by measure/weight, others by custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the classification of the six ribawi commodities and explain why nass overrides custom.

Core Idea
The six ribawi items are always by measure or weight; custom cannot change it.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that the six commodities mentioned in the hadith (barley, wheat, dates, salt, gold, silver) retain their classification as measured or weighed regardless of local custom. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya provides proof from the Sunnah and explains the superiority of textual evidence over customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State which commodities are classified as kayli (measured) and which as wazni (weighed) according to the Hanafi school.
The ruling is based on the explicit hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the specific hadith reference cited in the passage that supports the ruling.
The hadith of Ubada ibn al-Samit is referenced.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves that the classification is permanent and not subject to custom.
The explicit mention of measure for grains and weight for gold/silver.
4
Analyze the nass vs. 'urf argument
Understand why the text (nass) is considered stronger than custom ('urf) in this context.
Custom may be based on falsehood; nass is universally binding.
5
Apply to non-textual commodities
For commodities not mentioned in the hadith, custom determines the classification.
This is the rule for all other goods.

Source Text

كتاب البيع باب الربا
(والشعير، والبُرُّ، والتّمر، والملح كيلي، والذهب، والفضة وزني أبداً، وإن تُرِكا فيها) : أي وإن تُرِكَ الكيلُ في الأربعةِ المتقدمة، والوزن في الآخرين ؛ لقوله : «الحنطة بالحنطة ( الحديث ، ويُحْمَلُ في غيرها على العُرْف (1) قوله : لقوله ؛ حاصل الاستدلال أنَّ النبي ينص على تحريم التفاضل في الأربعة المتقدّمة كيلاً، وفي الآخرين وزناً، والنص أقوى من العرف ؛ لأن العرف جاز أن يكون على باطل ؛ كتعارف أهل زماننا في إخراج الشموع والسرج إلى المقابر في ليالي العيد حجية. والنص بعد ثبوته لا يحتمل أن يكون على باطل ؛ ولأن الـعــرف عـلـى الـذيـن تعارفوه والتزموه فقط، والنص حجَّةٌ على الكلِّ فهو أقوى ؛ ولأنَّ العرف صار حجَّةً بالنص، وهو قوله : «ما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن (٢)، كذا في «الفتح»(۳). والأقوى لا يتركُ بالأدنى، فكلُّ ما نص على تحريم التفاضل فيه كيلاً فهو كيلي دائماً، وإن ترك الناسُ الكيل فيه كالشعير والبر والتمر والملح، وكل ما نص على تحريم التفاضل فيه وزناً فهو موزون دائماً ، وإن ترك الناس الوزن فيه كالذهب والفضة. [٢]قوله : ويحملُ في غيرها...الخ ؛ يعني ما لا نص في كونه كيليّاً أو وزنيّاً يحملُ على العرف.
Book of Sales, Chapter of Riba: (And barley, wheat, dates, salt are by measure, and gold and silver are by weight always, even if they are abandoned in them) i.e., even if the measure is abandoned in the first four and weight in the other two, due to his statement: 'Wheat for wheat' hadith, and they are interpreted in others by custom. (1) His statement: due to his statement; the summary of the inference is that the Prophet explicitly prohibits surplus in the first four by measure and in the others by weight, and the text is stronger than custom. Because custom may be based on falsehood, like the custom of our time of taking candles and lamps to graveyards on the nights of Eid—no authority. And the text, after its establishment, cannot be based on falsehood. And because custom only binds those who adopt it, while the text is a proof for all, so it is stronger. And because custom becomes a proof by the text, and it is his statement: 'What the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah,' as in al-Fath. And the stronger is not abandoned for the weaker. So everything for which surplus is prohibited by measure is always by measure, even if people abandon measurement like barley, wheat, dates, salt; and everything for which surplus is prohibited by weight is always by weight, even if people abandon weight like gold and silver. [2] His statement: and it is interpreted in others...etc., meaning what has no text indicating it is by measure or weight is interpreted by custom.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage establishes a clear ruling regarding the six ribawi commodities mentioned in the hadith: barley, wheat, dates, salt, gold, and silver. They are always considered by measure (for the first four) or by weight (for gold and silver), irrespective of local custom. The proof is the explicit hadith which specifies measure for grains and weight for precious metals. The text (nass) is stronger than custom because custom may be based on falsehood and is not universally binding. The hadith 'What the Muslims see as good is good with Allah' is itself a proof that custom has authority, but only when it does not contradict explicit texts. Therefore, the nass takes precedence. For commodities not mentioned in the hadith, custom ('urf) determines whether they are measured or weighed. This is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah.

Key Terms
كَيْلِي (kayli): Something that is measured by volume/capacity, like grains.
وَزْنِي (wazni): Something that is measured by weight, like gold and silver.
العُرْف (al-'urf): Custom prevailing among people; used to determine the measure/weight of unspecified commodities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All commodities are based on local custom
B) The six named commodities follow the hadith; others follow custom
C) Only the six named commodities are considered; others are not subject to riba
D) It depends on the market practice

Key Takeaway
The six ribawi commodities are always measured or weighed as specified by the hadith, and custom cannot change their classification for riba purposes.

The Six Ribawi Items: Fixed Measures Over Custom
Ruling with proof from hadith, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the six ribawi items, explain the proof from hadith, and apply the rule to invalidate sales that deviate from the prescribed measure.

Core Idea
The six ribawi items are permanently measured by volume or weight by nass; custom cannot change them.

In this passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, the commentator explains that the six items mentioned in the riba hadith are perpetually classified as makil or mawzun. Even if people abandon measuring by volume or weight for these items, the legal rule remains. The proof is the hadith itself, which is stronger than custom. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf argued that custom could override, but the majority maintains the textual proof's supremacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that barley, wheat, dates, and salt are always makil (volume-measured), and gold and silver are always mawzun (weight-measured). This classification is perpetual, regardless of changing practices.
The ruling applies only to these six items; others follow custom.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the hadith: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand.' The hadith specifies the measure (kayl or wazn) for each category.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'like for like' (مثلاً بمثل) requires equivalence in the specific measure mentioned. Since the Prophet explicitly linked each item to its measure, that measure becomes the legal standard.
Textual proof (nass) is stronger than custom because it is established as a revelation.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that the original prescription was based on custom; therefore, if custom changes, the measure changes. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond that the Prophet's endorsement of the custom at that time amounts to a nass, so it cannot be overridden.
The majority view is mufta bihi; the passage supports it by saying 'the stronger is not abandoned for the weaker'.
5
Apply the rule to invalidate deviant sales
Selling wheat for wheat by weight or gold for gold by volume is invalid because equivalence in the prescribed measure is not assured. The condition of permissibility is equivalence in the measure specified by nass.
Even if both parties agree, the sale is invalid due to potential riba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب الربا
والشعير، والبر، والتمر، والملح كيلي ، والذهب، والفضة وزني أبداً ، وإن تُرِكا فيها
ويحمل في غيرها على العرف
(والشعير ، والبُرُّ ، والتّمر، والملح كيلي، والذهب، والفضة وزني أبداً، وإن تُرِكا فيها) : أي وإن تُرِكَ الكيلُ في الأربعةِ المتقدمة، والوزن في الآخرين ؛ لقوله : «الحنطة بالحنطة ( الحديث ، ويُحْمَلُ في غيرها على العُرْف. قوله : لقوله؛ حاصل الاستدلال أنَّ النبي ينص على تحريم التفاضل في الأربعة المتقدّمة كيلاً، وفي الآخرين وزناً، والنص أقوى من العرف؛ لأن العرف جاز أن يكون على باطل؛ كتعارف أهل زماننا في إخراج الشموع والسرج إلى المقابر في ليالي العيد حجية. والنص بعد ثبوته لا يحتمل أن يكون على باطل؛ ولأن الـعــرف عـلـى الـذيـن تعارفوه والتزموه فقط، والنص حجَّةٌ على الكلِّ فهو أقوى؛ ولأنَّ العرف صار حجَّةً بالنص، وهو قوله: «ما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن»، كذا في «الفتح». والأقوى لا يتركُ بالأدنى، فكلُّ ما نص على تحريم التفاضل فيه كيلاً فهو كيلي دائماً، وإن ترك الناسُ الكيل فيه كالشعير والبر والتمر والملح، وكل ما نص على تحريم التفاضل فيه وزناً فهو موزون دائماً، وإن ترك الناس الوزن فيه كالذهب والفضة. قوله : ويحملُ في غيرها...الخ؛ يعني ما لا نص في كونه كيليّاً أو وزنيّاً يحمل على العرف وعاداتِ الناس كغيرِ الستَّةِ المذكورة؛ لأنَّ عادة الناس دالة على جواز الحكم فيما وقعت عليه عادتهم، لقوله: «ما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن». كذا في «النهاية». وعن أبي يوسف الله: إنه يعتبر العرف على خلاف المنصوص عليه، أيضاً أنَّ النص بالكيل في المكيل، وبالوزن في الموزون في ذلك الوقت، إنما كان لمكان العادة، فكانت العادة هي المنظورة إليها وقد تبدلت. والجواب عنه: إن تقرير رسول الله الله إياهم على ما تعارفوا في ذلك بمنزلة النص منه، فلا يعتبر بالعرف؛ لأنَّه لا يعارض النص، كذا في «الكفاية). قوله : فلم يجز؛ تفريع على كون الأربعةِ المذكورة من المكيلات والآخرين من الموزونات، فلو باع البرَّ بالبرِّ متساوياً ووزناً، أو باع الذهب بالذهب متساوياً كيلاً لا يجوز عند الطرفين، وإن تعارفوا ذلك؛ لأنَّ شرط الجواز فيهما المماثلة في الـكـيـل والوزن، ولم يعلم، فتوهّم الفضلُ على ما هو المعيار فيه، وهو الكيلُ في البر، والوزن في الذهب.
فلم يَجُز بيعُ البُرِّ بالبُرِّ متساوياً وزناً، والذهب بجنسه متساوياً كيلاً كما لم يجز مجازفة
Book of Sales, Chapter of Riba. And barley, wheat, dates, and salt are (always) measured by volume, and gold and silver are (always) measured by weight forever, even if they are abandoned in them (i.e., even if people abandon using volume or weight for them). And other than them (i.e., other items) are to be determined by custom. (And barley, wheat, dates, and salt are measured by volume, and gold and silver are measured by weight forever, even if they are abandoned in them): i.e., even if measuring by volume is abandoned for the first four, and measuring by weight is abandoned for the latter two, due to his saying: 'Wheat for wheat' (the hadith). And other than them are to be determined by custom. His saying: 'due to his saying' — the gist of the inference is that the Prophet explicitly forbids excess in the first four by volume and in the latter two by weight, and the textual proof (nass) is stronger than custom, because custom may be based on falsehood, like the custom of our time of taking candles and lamps to graves on the nights of 'Eid (which is baseless). And textual proof after its establishment cannot be based on falsehood. Also because custom only applies to those who practice and adopt it, while textual proof is a proof for everyone, so it is stronger. Also because custom became a proof through textual proof, namely his saying: 'What the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah,' as in al-Fath. And the stronger is not abandoned for the weaker. So everything for which excess is textually forbidden by volume is a volume-measured item perpetually, even if people abandon measuring by volume for it, like barley, wheat, dates, and salt. And everything for which excess is textually forbidden by weight is a weight-measured item perpetually, even if people abandon measuring by weight for it, like gold and silver. His saying: 'And other than them are to be determined by custom' etc.: meaning that what has no textual proof as being volume-measured or weight-measured is to be determined by custom and people's practices, like other than the mentioned six, because people's practice indicates the permissibility of the ruling regarding that which their practice covers, due to his saying: 'What the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah.' As in al-Nihaya. And from Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him): that custom is considered contrary to the textual proof, also that the textual proof for volume in volume-measured items and weight in weight-measured items at that time was due to custom, so custom was the primary consideration and it has changed. The response to him: that the Prophet's (peace be upon him) endorsement of their practice in that regard is like a textual proof from him, so it is not overridden by custom, because it does not contradict the textual proof. As in al-Kifaya. His saying: 'So it is not permissible' is a branching off from the fact that the four mentioned are among volume-measured items and the other two among weight-measured items. So if one sells wheat for wheat equally by weight, or sells gold for its kind equally by volume, it is not permissible according to both parties, even if they customarily do that, because the condition of permissibility in both is equivalence in volume and weight, and it is not known (that equivalence is achieved), thus excess is assumed based on the standard for it, which is volume for wheat and weight for gold. So it is not permissible to sell wheat for wheat equally by weight, and gold for its kind equally by volume, just as it is not permissible to sell by guess (mujazafah).
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from hadith. It establishes that six specific ribawi goods (barley, wheat, dates, salt, gold, silver) are perpetually classified as makil (volume-measured) or mawzun (weight-measured) regardless of changing customs. The Sharh explains that the textual proof (nass) from the famous riba hadith is stronger than custom, so even if people stop using volume or weight for these items, their legal classification remains. Custom is only considered for items not explicitly mentioned in the hadith, as per the hadith 'What the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah.' There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf held that custom could override the textual proof because the original prescription was based on custom, but the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) maintain that the Prophet's endorsement amounts to a textual proof. The passage then applies the rule: selling wheat by weight or gold by volume is invalid because equivalence in the prescribed measure is not assured, leading to potential riba.

Key Terms
كيلي (kayli): An item whose legal measure (in exchange and zakah) is by volume (kayl), not weight.
وزني (wazni): An item whose legal measure is by weight (wazn).
عرف ('urf): Custom or common practice that is consistent and widespread; used to determine measure for items not explicitly mentioned in the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if people start weighing wheat instead of measuring by volume, what is the ruling on selling wheat for wheat by weight?
A) Permissible because custom has changed the standard.
B) Not permissible because wheat is permanently a makil item based on nass.
C) Permissible only if both parties agree.
D) Not permissible because weight is always an invalid measure for wheat.

Key Takeaway
The six ribawi items are perpetually measured by their prescribed standard based on nass, overriding any change in custom.

Salam in Wheat by Weight: Custom Overrides Nass
Explaining that salam is permitted in wheat by weight despite its kilay nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in wheat by weight and explain the rational basis (waṣf al-‘illa) that distinguishes it from the riba prohibition.

Core Idea
In salam, the measure that prevents dispute is what matters, not the riba measure.

This passage tackles an apparent conflict: wheat is a ribawi item measured by volume (makīl), so why is it permissible to contract a forward sale (salam) for wheat by weight? The Hanafi jurists reconcile this by identifying the true purpose of specification in salam—avoiding future dispute—and holding that any precise measure, including weight, fulfills that purpose. Custom has settled on weight, and the fatwa follows custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the exception
The passage begins with an exception (illā annahu yaʿmalun...). State the general rule and the specific exception: salam in wheat by weight is permissible even though wheat is normally volume-measured.
General rule: ribawi items like wheat must be exchanged with equivalence in volume. Exception: salam is exempt from that equivalence condition.
2
Locate the proof and its structure
The proof is not a text but an analogy (qiyās jaliyy). Identify the original ruling (aṣl) and the new case (farʿ). The aṣl is specification by volume, and the farʿ is specification by weight.
The ‘illa (effective cause) is established from the purpose of salam: to make the item known in a way that precludes dispute.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah (how the proof applies)
Explain why weight is analogous to volume: both provide a precise, objective measure that eliminates uncertainty. The passage explicitly says 'just as this is achieved by volume, it is achieved by mentioning weight.'
This is a qiyās jaliyy: the ‘illa (known measure) is present in both.
4
Note the intra-Hanafī ikhtilāf and the tarjīḥ
Al-Hasan ibn Ziyād reported a contrary position: wheat is makīl by nass, so weight cannot substitute. The passage then states the fatwa is on the first opinion (al-awwal) due to people's custom. Identify the authority (al-Kifāya) and the weight given to custom.
Custom (‘urf) can override a weaker analogy or a transmitted (nawādir) opinion when it does not contradict a clear text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أنه يجوز الإسلام في البُرّ ونحوه وزناً؛ لوجود الإسلام في معلوم، فإنَّ المماثلة في الوزن ليست بمعتبرة في السَّلَم، وإنّما المعتبر فيه هو الإعلام على وجه ينفي المنازعة في التسليم، وذلك كما يحصلُ بالكيل يحصل بذكر الوزن، كذا صرح به العلامة العيني وهذا رواية الطحاوي الله عن أصحابنا، وروى الحسن له عن أصحابنا أنه لا يجوز؛ لأنه مكيل بالنص، والفتوى على الأوّل لعادةِ الناس. كذا في «الكفاية»، وغيرها.

Thus al-'Allama al-'Ayni explicitly stated it. And this is the riwaya of al-Tahawi from our companions. And al-Hasan (ibn Ziyad) narrated from our companions that it is not permissible because it is (textually) a volume-measured item. But the fatwa is on the first (opinion) due to people's custom. As in al-Kifaya and others.

Commentary
This passage provides a specific exception to the general rule: although wheat is a makil ribawi item, it is permissible to contract a salam (forward sale) for wheat by specifying the weight. The reasoning is that salam requires the subject matter to be known in a way that prevents dispute, and weight serves that purpose just as well as volume. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: al-Hasan ibn Ziyad transmitted that it is not permissible because wheat is makil by nass, but the fatwa is on the permissibility due to established custom. This ruling is from the later Hanafi authorities (mutakhkhirin) who gave weight to custom in salam contracts.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance and the goods are delivered later; the goods must be specified in a way that avoids dispute.
معلوم (ma'lum): The subject matter in salam must be known (specified) in terms of type, quantity, and quality to prevent future disputes.

Key Takeaway

Custom vs. Text: Selling Wheat by Weight
Intra-Hanafi dispute on custom vs. text in riba exchanges.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on whether custom can override an explicit textual ruling regarding the standard measure for ribawi items.

Core Idea
The Prophet's tacit approval textualized the custom; a text cannot be overridden by later custom.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the role of custom in determining the standard measure for ribawi items. The question: can a widespread custom of selling wheat by weight override the established ruling that wheat must be exchanged by measure? Abu Yusuf argues yes, citing the hadith 'What the Muslims see as good is good with Allah.' The response from the matn and the commentary defends the text's sanctity, showing how the Prophet's taqrir elevated custom to the level of nass. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the hierarchy of legal sources in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Basis
The base text rules that selling wheat for wheat by weight is invalid. Why? Because the condition for valid exchange of ribawi items of the same genus is equivalence in the recognized standard (kayl for wheat, wazn for gold).
The ruling applies to all six ribawi items mentioned in the hadith.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's Argument
Abu Yusuf argues that the original textual ruling was based on custom; since custom has changed, the ruling should change. He cites the hadith: 'ما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن'.
This hadith is used to support the idea that communal practice has normative weight.
3
Examine the Hanafi Response
The response asserts that the Prophet's tacit approval (taqrir) of the custom at that time made it equivalent to a textual ruling (bi manzilat al-nass). Custom cannot oppose a text.
The taqrir is considered a form of revelation (wahy) in Hanafi usul.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: Abu Hanifa says the sale is invalid (fasid) because the condition of equivalence in the prescribed measure is missing. Abu Yusuf says it is valid if custom dictates.
The fatwa is on the first position, but the existence of the dispute shows the nuanced role of custom.
5
Note the Fatwa Ruling
The relied-upon fatwa is on the first position (invalid), as stated in al-Kifayah: 'wal-fatwa `ala al-awwal li `adati al-nas.' However, the phrase 'li `adati al-nas' indicates that even the first position is influenced by custom.
This shows that custom is not entirely disregarded; it plays a role in tarjih.

Source Text

على العرف وعاداتِ الناس كغيرِ الستَّةِ المذكورة ؛ لأنَّ عادة الناس دالة على جواز الحكم فيما وقعت عليه عادتهم، لقوله : «ما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن». كذا في «النهاية». وعن أبي يوسف : إنه يعتبر العرف على خلاف المنصوص عليه، أيضاً أنَّ النص بالكيل في المكيل، وبالوزن في الموزون في ذلك الوقت، إنما كان لمكان العادة ، فكانت العادة هي المنظورة إليها وقد تبدلت. والجواب عنه : إن تقرير رسول الله إياهم على ما تعارفوا في ذلك بمنزلة النص منه ، فلا يعتبر بالعرف ؛ لأنَّه لا يعارض النص، كذا في «الكفاية). قوله : فلم يجز ؛ تفريع على كون الأربعةِ المذكورة من المكيلات والآخرين من الموزونات ، فلو باع البرَّ بالبرِّ متساوياً ووزناً ، أو باع الذهب بالذهب متساوياً كيلاً لا يجوز عند الطرفين، وإن تعارفوا ذلك ؛ لأنَّ شرط الجواز فيهما المماثلة في الـكـيـل والوزن، ولم يعلم، فتوهّم الفضلُ على ما هو المعيار فيه، وهو الكيلُ في البر، والوزن في الذهب. إلا أنه يجوز الإسلام في البُرّ ونحوه وزناً ؛ لوجود الإسلام في معلوم، فإنَّ المماثلة في الوزن ليست بمعتبرة في السَّلَم، وإنّما المعتبر فيه هو الإعلام على وجه ينفي المنازعة في التسليم، وذلك كما يحصلُ بالكيل يحصل بذكر الوزن، كذا صرح به العلامة العيني وهذا رواية الطحاوي عن أصحابنا، وروى الحسن عن أصحابنا أنه لا يجوز؛ لأنه مكيل بالنص، والفتوى على الأوّل لعادةِ الناس. كذا في «الكفاية» وغيرها.
Thus it is not permissible to sell wheat for wheat equally by weight, nor gold for its kind equally by measure, just as it is not permissible by estimation. Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the role of custom ('urf) in determining the standard measure for ribawi transactions. The ruling states that selling wheat (a measured item) by weight rather than measure is invalid, as is selling gold (a weighed item) by measure. The commentator notes that some argue custom should prevail, citing the hadith 'What the Muslims see as good is good with Allah.' Abu Yusuf holds that the original textual ruling was based on custom, and since custom has changed, the standard should change accordingly. The response from Abu Hanifa's position (via the text) is that the Prophet's tacit approval of the custom at that time effectively textualized it, so custom cannot override the explicit text. The commentary then clarifies that the ruling is derived from the principle that ribawi items must be exchanged with equivalence in their recognized standard (kayl for wheat, wazn for gold). An exception is made for salam (forward sale), where weight is permissible because the condition is specification, not equivalence. The fatwa follows the first view (that such sales are invalid) due to the dominance of custom, but the dispute remains on the level of tarjih.

Key Terms
العرف (al-`urf): Custom or habitual practice of people, considered as a legal source in the absence of explicit text.
المماثلة (al-mumathalah): Equivalence in the prescribed standard (kayl for wheat, wazn for gold) required to avoid riba al-fadl.
السلم (al-salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for a specified commodity to be delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the hadith prohibits selling wheat by weight.
B) Because the condition of equivalence in the standard measure (kayl) is not met, and custom cannot override the text.
C) Because the parties did not intend a valid sale.
D) Because salam is required for such transactions.

Key Takeaway
Custom cannot override an explicit text, especially when the Prophet's tacit approval has elevated the custom to the level of a revealed ruling.

Specification and Hand-to-Hand in Riba Sales
Ruling on ta'yin and qabd in ribawi sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for specification and hand-to-hand exchange in ribawi sales according to the Hanafi school and identify when hand-to-hand is required.

Core Idea
In non-sarf ribawi sales, specification is required but hand-to-hand is not; in sarf, both are required.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common question: when is hand-to-hand exchange necessary in ribawi transactions? The Hanafi school distinguishes between currency exchange (sarf) and other ribawi items like wheat and barley. Understanding this distinction prevents invalid contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the main ruling
Identify the general rule: in ribawi sales, the sold item must be specified (mu'ayyan). If not, the contract is treated as salam with its own conditions.
Specification avoids gharar and ensures the precise object of sale.
2
Distinguish between sarf and non-sarf
Note that hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in the session is not required for ribawi sales except when the transaction involves gold and silver (sarf). This is a key distinction.
For non-sarf, the goods may be absent as long as they exist and are owned.
3
Analyze the examples
Work through the commentary's three scenarios: both items specific, one item a debt as price, and one item a debt as sold good. Understand why each is valid or invalid.
When debt is the price, receipt before separation is necessary; when debt is the sold item, it is invalid even if brought to the session.
4
Identify the proof
The passage cites the hadith 'Gold for gold is riba except...' to establish the hand-to-hand condition in sarf. Recognize that the proof is a hadith, and its implication is that for non-sarf, the condition is absent.
The hadith is a hadith ahad, but it is accepted in this context.

And it is considered that specification (ta'yin) in riba [transactions] other than currency exchange (sarf) is without the condition of hand-to-hand exchange. The consideration in the sale of ribawi goods is that the sold item be specified (mu`ayyan). If it is not specified, it becomes salam, so its conditions are necessary. If the conditions of salam are not met, the contract is a sale that is not salam, so specification is necessary. Thus hand-to-hand exchange in the session is not required if it is not sarf; if it is sarf, it is required. He said: 'And it is considered...' etc.: When two parties exchange a measured item for a measured item, or a weighed item for a weighed item, both of the same genus or different genera, the sale is not valid unless both are specific goods (`ayn) to which the contract is added. Whether present or absent, as long as it exists in his ownership before separation (before the parties part physically) is not a condition for validity except in gold and silver. If one is a specific good and the other is a debt (dayn) described in the liability, then it is considered: if the debt is made the price and the specific good is sold, the sale is valid on condition that the debt becomes specified (by receipt) before they separate. If the debt is made the sold item, it is not valid even if he brings the debt in the session, because he is selling what he does not possess. For example: if he says, 'I sell you this wheat as a qafiz for a qafiz of good wheat,' or 'I sell you this wheat as a qafiz for a qafiz of good barley,' the sale is valid because he made the specific good the sold item and the described debt the price. But receipt of the debt before separation is a condition because the condition for validity is that it be a sale of a specific good for a specific good, and what is a debt is not specified except by receipt. If he receives the debt and then they separate, the sale is valid whether he received the specific good or not. If he says, 'I bought from you a qafiz of good wheat for this qafiz of wheat,' or 'I bought from you a qafiz of good barley for this qafiz of wheat,' it is not valid even if he brings the debt in the session, because he made the debt a sold item, becoming a seller of what is not in his possession, which is not valid. Thus in 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq'. He said: 'it is required' means hand-to-hand exchange in the session, due to his saying: 'Gold for gold is riba except'.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage states the legal rule that in ribawi transactions, the goods must be specified (ta`yin). If not specified, the contract is considered salam, which has its own conditions. The key point is that hand-to-hand exchange (qabd) in the session is not required unless the transaction is sarf (exchange of gold for silver or silver for gold). The commentary then expands with examples: If both items are specific goods (`ayn), the sale is valid without hand-to-hand exchange (except for gold/silver). If one item is a debt (dayn) described in the liability, then if the debt is the price, the sale is valid provided the debt is received before the parties separate. If the debt is the sold item, the sale is invalid because one would be selling what one does not possess. The commentary provides concrete examples using wheat and barley. Finally, the requirement for hand-to-hand exchange in sarf is supported by the hadith: 'Gold for gold is riba except hand to hand' (the text cuts off).

Key Terms
التعيين (al-ta`yin): Specification of the actual goods in a sale, as opposed to a debt or general description.
التقابض (al-taqabud): Hand-to-hand exchange of the counter-values in the sale session.
الصرف (al-sarf): Exchange of gold for silver or silver for gold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale of wheat for barley (both measured items), is hand-to-hand exchange in the session required for validity according to the passage?
A) Yes, because both are ribawi items.
B) No, because the condition of hand-to-hand is only for sarf (gold/silver).
C) Yes, because the hadith requires it.
D) No, but specification of the goods is required instead.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, specification of goods is mandatory in ribawi sales to distinguish from salam, and hand-to-hand exchange is only required when dealing with gold or silver (sarf).

Specification and Hand-to-Hand Exchange in Ribawi Sales
Explains when ta'yin is necessary and when taqabud is not in ribawi transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whether hand-to-hand exchange is required in a given ribawi sale and apply the Hanafi rule that specification is necessary in non-sarf transactions.

Core Idea
In non-sarf ribawi sales, specification is required but hand-to-hand is not; only in sarf is both required.

This lesson clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh of sales: when trading ribawi goods, the requirement of hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) depends on whether the transaction is sarf (exchange of gold/silver) or not. The passage explains that in non-sarf sales, the sold item must be specified (ta'yin), but immediate mutual receipt is not necessary. Instead, the focus is on the specificity of the commodity. Through detailed examples with wheat and barley, you will learn how this rule applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage begins by stating that in non-sarf ribawi sales, specification (ta'yin) is required, and hand-to-hand exchange is not a condition. Distinguish this from sarf where taqabud is required.
Key terms: ta'yin = specification; taqabud = hand-to-hand exchange.
2
Examine the exception for salam
If the sold item is not specified, the contract defaults to salam, which has its own conditions. If those conditions are not met, the sale is invalid due to lack of specification.
Salam is a forward sale with prepayment; it requires specific conditions like full payment at session and delivery at a future date.
3
Apply the rule to different combinations
Work through the examples: when both items are specific (عين), the sale is valid regardless of hand-to-hand. When one is specific and the other is a debt (دين), the sale is valid only if the debt is specified by receipt before parting. When the debt is made the sold item, the sale is invalid.
The preposition 'باء' (baa) indicates price; what follows it is the price, and what comes before is the sold item.
4
Summarize the practical distinction
Thus, in non-sarf ribawi sales, hand-to-hand exchange is not required; only specification is necessary. In sarf (gold/silver exchange), both specification and hand-to-hand are required.
This distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i school, which requires hand-to-hand in all food sales.

كتاب البيع باب الربا واعتبر تعيين الربا في غير صرف بلا شرط التقابض المعتبر في بيع الأموال الربوية أن يكون المبيع معيناً حتى لو لم يكن معينا كان سَلَماً فَلا بُدَّ فيه من شرائطه وإذا لم يُوجَدْ شرائط السَّلَم كان العقد بيعاً غيرَ سَلَم فلا بُدَّ من التعيين فلا يُشْتَرطُ التَّقابض في المجلس إن لم يكن صرفاً حتى لو كان صرفاً يشترط. فإذا تبايعا كيلياً بكيلي أو وزنياً بوزني كلاهما من جنس واحد أو من جنسين مختلفين فإنَّ البيع لا يجوز حتى يكون كلاهما عيناً أضيف إليه العقد وهو حاضر أو غائب بعد أن يكون موجودا في ملكه قبل الافتراق بالأبدان ليس بشرط لجوازه إلا في الذهب والفضة. ولو كان أحدهما عيناً وأضيف إليه العقد والآخر ديناً موصوفاً في الذمة فإنّه ينظر إن جعل الدين منهما ثمناً والعين مبيعاً جاز البيع بشرط أن يتعين الدين منهما قبل التفرق بالأبدان وإن جعل الدين منهما مبيعاً لا يجوز وإن أحضره في المجلس والذي ذكر فيه الباء ثمن وما لم يدخل في الباء مبيع. وبيانه : إذا قال: بعتك هذه الحنطة على أنها قفيز بقفيز حنطة جيدة أو قال : بعت منك هذه الحنطة على أنها قفيز بقفيز من شعير جيد فالبيع جائز ; لأنه جعل العين منهما بيعاً والدين الموصوف ثمناً ولكن قبض الدين منهما قبل التفرق بالأبدان شرط ; لأنَّ من شرط جواز هذا البيع أن يجعلَ عن عين بعين وما كان ديناً لا يتعين إلا بالقبض. ولو قبض الدين منهما ثم تفرَّقَ جاز البيع قبضَ العين منهما أو لم يقبض ولو قال : اشتريتُ منك قفيز حنطة جيّدة بهذا القفيز من الحنطة أو قال : اشتريت منك قفير شعير جيد بهذا القفيز من الحنطة فإنّه لا يجوز وإن أحضر الدين في المجلس ; لأنه جعل الدين مبيعاً فصار بائعاً ما ليس عنده وهو لا يجوز كذا في «البحر الرائق»).
And the specification of riba is required in non-sarf [transactions] without the condition of hand-to-hand exchange. The consideration in selling ribawi goods is that the sold item be specified, so that if it is not specified, it is a salam [sale], so its conditions are necessary. And if the conditions of salam are not found, the contract is a sale that is not salam, so specification is necessary. Thus, hand-to-hand exchange is not required in the session if it is not sarf. So if it is sarf, it is required. Explanation: If two parties exchange a measured item for a measured item, or a weighed item for a weighed item, both of the same genus or of different genera, the sale is not valid unless both are a specific [commodity] to which the contract is attached, either present or absent, as long as it exists in his ownership. The condition of before parting with bodies is not required for its validity except in gold and silver. If one is a specific commodity and the other is a debt described in the liability, then it is considered: if the debt is made as the price and the specific commodity as the sold item, the sale is valid on condition that the debt be specified before parting with bodies. If the debt is made as the sold item, it is not valid even if he brings it in the session. And what is mentioned with the preposition 'baa' is the price, and what is not included in 'baa' is the sold item. Explanation: If he says: 'I sold you this wheat on condition that it is one qafiz for one qafiz of good wheat' or says: 'I sold you this wheat on condition that it is one qafiz for one qafiz of good barley', the sale is valid because he made the specific commodity among them the sold item and the described debt as the price. But the receipt of the debt before parting with bodies is a condition because one of the conditions for validity of this sale is that it be for a specific [commodity] for a specific [commodity]. And what is a debt does not become specific except with receipt. If he receives the debt and then they part, the sale is valid whether he received the specific commodity or not. If he says: 'I bought from you one qafiz of good wheat for this qafiz of wheat' or says: 'I bought from you one qafiz of good barley for this qafiz of wheat', it is not valid even if he brings the debt in the session because he made the debt the sold item, thus becoming a seller of what he does not have, which is not valid. So it is in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on the requirement of specification (ta'yin) in ribawi transactions and the condition of hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud). The author begins by stating that in non-sarf ribawi sales, the sold item must be specified. If it is not specified, the contract becomes a salam contract, which has its own conditions. If salam conditions are not met, the contract is invalid for lack of specification. In such sales, hand-to-hand exchange is not required unless the transaction is sarf (exchange of gold and silver). Then he provides detailed examples: if both items are specific goods, the sale is valid with or without hand-to-hand exchange. If one is specific and the other is a debt, it is valid only if the debt is specified through receipt before parting. If the debt is made the sold item, it is invalid. The commentary illustrates these scenarios with examples of wheat and barley sales.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the exact commodity being sold, as opposed to a generic description.
صرف (sarf): The exchange of gold and silver (currency) for gold and silver.
تقابض (taqabud): Mutual physical receipt of the exchanged items in the session of contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi sale of wheat for barley, both specified and present, which of the following is a requirement for validity?
A) Hand-to-hand exchange in the session.
B) The sold item must be specified.
C) Both items must be of the same genus.
D) The price must be gold or silver.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, non-sarf ribawi sales require specification of the commodity but not hand-to-hand exchange; only sarf requires immediate mutual receipt.

Taqabud in Ribawi Sales: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on taqabud in ribawi food sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on taqabud in non-sarf ribawi sales, explain the Hanafi interpretation of 'yadan bi yad', and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In non-sarf ribawi sales, specification (ta'yin) suffices; hand-to-hand receipt is not required.

The requirement of hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in the session for ribawi food sales is a point of contention between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position, focusing on the interpretation of the famous hadith 'hand to hand' and the underlying legal principles. By understanding the Hanafi argument that specification replaces physical receipt, you will see how a single textual phrase can yield divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Ruling
State the exact point of divergence: Does the sale of wheat for barley (different genus, both ribawi) require hand-to-hand exchange in the session for validity?
The Hanafi school says no; the Shafi'i school says yes.
2
Examine the Shafi'i Proof
Analyze the Shafi'i dalil: the hadith 'hand to hand' interpreted literally as physical receipt, and the concern that sequential receipt creates suspicion of riba.
Note the argument that suspicion in riba is treated like reality.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Understand the Hanafi counter: the items are already specific (mu'ayyan), so receipt is not required; analogy to selling a specific garment for another. Interpret 'yadan bi yad' as 'ainan bi 'ain (specific for specific).
Reference the hadith of 'Ubada ibn al-Samit as support.
4
Contrast with Sarf
Note the exception: in sarf (exchange of gold/silver), taqabud is required because those items are not specific without receipt. This distinction is key to the Hanafi position.
Sarf's requirement does not contradict the general rule.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
State the thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi, a sale of wheat for barley without handover is valid; under Shafi'i it is invalid. This affects everyday transactions.
The ruling has real impact on market practice.

According to al-Shafi'i, hand-to-hand exchange is required in the session in the sale of food, whether sold with its genus or other than its genus. This concerns ribawi goods. As for other [goods], if they are not specified, if they are subject to salam, if its conditions are met, it is valid with its conditions via salam. If not found, the sale is invalid. If it is not subject to salam, the sale is invalid due to lack of specification. 'Take and take, and silver for silver is riba except take and take, and wheat for wheat is riba except take and take.' Reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah, mentioned by al-Zayla'i in Takhrij al-Hidayah. 'Ha' is built on fatha meaning 'take'. Each of the seller and buyer says 'ha' and they exchange, meaning hand to hand before parting of bodies. The statement: 'hand-to-hand exchange is required' etc. because the statement 'hand to hand' in the famous accepted hadith is interpreted figuratively for receipt, as the hand is the instrument of receipt. And because if they do not take receipt, the receipts may be sequential, and it is apparent that cash has a superiority over others, so the suspicion of riba arises, and suspicion is like reality in the matter of riba. This is also the view of Malik and Ahmad. And our [Hanafi] argument: that each of them is a specific sold item, so its receipt is not required as if one sold a specific garment for a specific garment, unlike sarf, because in sarf it becomes specific only with receipt. As for the statement 'hand to hand', its meaning is 'specific for specific', because the hand is the instrument of specification as it is the instrument of receipt, so interpreting it as specification is more appropriate because of what 'Ubada ibn al-Samit narrated: 'specific for specific'. As for the sequential receipt, merchants do not differentiate in [creditworthiness] between what is received in the session and what is not received as long as it is prompt, unlike the case of present and deferred where they differentiate. This is the gist of what they said in this matter. The statement: 'whether sold with its genus or other' etc., for the sale of a measure of wheat for a measure of wheat, or a measure of barley or dates, and they part from...
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school regarding the requirement of hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in the sale of ribawi goods. The Shafi'i school, alongside Malik and Ahmad, requires hand-to-hand exchange in the session for all food sales, whether same genus or different, based on the hadith 'hand to hand' which they interpret as requiring physical receipt. The Hanafi school responds by arguing that each item in a non-sarf sale is already specified (mu'ayyan), so receipt is not required, analogous to a sale of a specific garment for another specific garment. The hadith 'hand to hand' is interpreted by Hanafis as meaning 'specific for specific' ('ainan bi 'ain), not physical handover, as the hand is also an instrument of specification. The passage concludes by noting that merchants do not distinguish between receipt in the session and later receipt when the payment is prompt, thus rejecting the analogy to time value.

Key Terms
تقابض (taqabud): Mutual physical receipt of the exchanged items in the session.
يدا بيد (yadan bi yad): Literally 'hand to hand', interpreted by Hanafis as 'specific for specific' ('ainan bi 'ain).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the hadith says so.
B) Because both items are specific commodities, unlike sarf.
C) Because merchants allow it.
D) Because barley is not ribawi.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) is not required for non-sarf ribawi food sales because specification (ta'yin) fulfills the purpose of preventing riba.

Hand-to-Hand Exchange in Ribawi Sales: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on immediate exchange requirement in ribawi sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not require immediate hand-to-hand exchange in the sale of specific ribawi goods, and contrast this with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
In specific goods, delay in exchange does not create riba; the hand specifies, not merely delivers.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether immediate hand-to-hand exchange (taqābuḍ) is required when selling ribawi items. The disagreement hinges on the interpretation of the hadith 'yadan bi yad'. Understanding this difference clarifies the Hanafi ruling on selling specific goods for specific goods without immediate delivery.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds that hand-to-hand exchange is not required when both items are specific (mu‘ayyan). The sale is valid even without immediate delivery.
This is based on the analogy with selling a specific garment for a specific garment.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Recognise that al-Shafi'i (along with Malik and Ahmad) requires immediate hand-to-hand exchange in the same session for all ribawi items, whether sold for like or unlike kind.
They interpret 'yadan bi yad' as physical delivery.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument: the hadith 'hā’ hā’' and 'yadan bi yad' command immediate exchange, and sequential taking creates a suspicion of riba.
They consider this suspicion as equivalent to actual riba in this context.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi reinterpretation: 'yadan bi yad' means 'specific for specific' ('aynan bi ‘ayn'), citing the narration of ‘Ubādah ibn al-Ṣāmit. The hand is an instrument of specification, not just delivery.
Merchants do not differentiate between taken and not-taken as long as both are immediate (ḥāl).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Under Hanafi, a seller can sell a specific bag of wheat for a specific bag of barley without immediate exchange; under Shafi'i, the sale would be invalid if not exchanged hand-to-hand.
Currency exchange (ṣarf) is an exception because it is not specified except by taking.

[1] قوله: يشترط التقابض...الخ؛ لأن قوله: «يداً بيد» في الحديث المشهور المتلقى بالقبول، يراد به القبضُ كناية، فكون اليد آلة للقبض؛ ولأنه إذا لم يتقابضا فقد يتعاقب القبضان، وظاهر أنّ للنقد مزيَّةً على غيره فيثبت شبهة الربا، والشبهة كالحقيقة في باب الربا، وهذا قول مالك وأحمد له أيضاً. ولنا: إنَّ كلا منهما مبيع متعين، فلا يشترط قبضه كما إذا باع ثوباً معيناً بثوبِ معين، بخلاف الصرف، فإنّه لا يتعيّنُ فيه إلا بالقبض، وأما قوله: «يدا بيد»، فمعناه عيناً بعين، إذ اليد آلة التعيين، كما هي آلة القبض فحمله على التعيين أولى، لما روى عبادة بن الصامت رضي الله عنه: « عيناً بعين ». وأما تعاقب القبض فالتجَّارُ لا يفصلون في المالية بين المقبوض في المجلس وغير المقبوض بعد أن يكون حالاً بخلاف الحال والمؤجل، فإنّهم يفصلون فيهما، هذا محصل ما قالوا في هذا المقام.
And according to al-Shafi'i, hand-to-hand exchange in the sitting is required in the sale of food, whether sold for its own kind or a different kind. This is for ribawi goods. As for non-ribawi goods, if they are not specified, if they are of the type in which salam can be made, then if the conditions of salam are found, the sale is valid with its conditions via salam; if not found, the sale is invalid; and if salam cannot be made in it, the sale is invalid for lack of specification. 'Take! Take! And silver for silver is riba except take! Take! And wheat for wheat is riba except take! Take!' – narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba, mentioned by al-Zayla'i in Takhrij al-Hidaya. 'Ha' is built on fatha meaning 'take'. Each of the seller and buyer says 'Ha' and they exchange, so its meaning is hand-to-hand before separation of bodies. [1] He said: 'He requires the exchange... etc.' because his statement 'hand to hand' in the famous hadith accepted by the community is intended as a metaphor for taking, since the hand is the instrument of taking; and because if they do not exchange hand-to-hand, then the two takings may be sequential, and it is apparent that cash has an advantage over other things, so the suspicion of riba arises, and suspicion is like reality in the chapter of riba. This is also the saying of Malik and Ahmad. And for us (Hanafi): each of them is a specific sold item, so its taking is not required, just as if one sold a specific garment for a specific garment, contrary to currency exchange, for it is not specified except by taking. Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the requirement of hand-to-hand exchange (تقابض) in the sale of ribawi items. The text first states the Shafi'i position: for food items, whether sold for like or unlike kind, immediate exchange is required in the sitting. For non-ribawi items that are unspecified, they require the conditions of salam. The Shafi'i basis is the hadith 'هاء وهاء' and 'يدا بيد', which they interpret as requiring immediate physical delivery to avoid the suspicion of riba. The Hanafi response (ولنا) argues that when each item is specific (مبيع متعين), such as a garment for a garment, no immediate exchange is required, unlike currency exchange where specification only occurs by taking. The Hanafi interpretation of 'يدا بيد' is 'عيناً بعين' (specific for specific), citing the narration of Ubadah ibn al-Samit. They further argue that merchants do not differentiate between taken and non-taken items as long as both are immediate (حال), so the suspicion of riba does not arise. This clarifies the Hanafi position that for specific goods, delay in exchange does not invalidate the sale.

Key Terms
تقابض (taqābuḍ): Hand-to-hand exchange, immediate physical delivery of both countervalues in a sale transaction
يدا بيد (yadan bi yad): Literally 'hand to hand'; interpreted by Shafi'i as immediate delivery, by Hanafi as 'specific for specific'
ربا (ribā): Usury or interest; prohibited increase in exchange of certain commodities

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because each garment is specific (mu‘ayyan), and specification removes the need for immediate delivery
C) Because the hadith 'يدا بيد' is weak
D) Because garments are considered currency

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that for specific (mu‘ayyan) goods, immediate hand-to-hand exchange is not required, interpreting 'yadan bi yad' as 'specific for specific'.

Selling a Fils for Two Fils and Meat for an Animal
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of selling specific fils for two fils and meat for same-kind animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of exchanging specific fils or meat for a same-kind animal and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Parties can nullify the conventional price-ness of fils and treat them as commodities, making a 1:2 exchange valid.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether selling a specific fils for two specific fils is valid. Imam Muhammad argues it leads to riba because fils are universally considered prices. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that parties can redefine fils as commodities, making the exchange permissible. The same principle applies to selling meat for an animal of the same kind.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn states 'وجاز' (it is permissible). Recognize that this is the relied-upon position in the text.
2
State Imam Muhammad's position and proof
Imam Muhammad forbids selling a specific fils for two fils because fils are universally considered prices (أثمان) and cannot be specified; thus it resembles riba.
He analogizes to selling a dirham for two dirhams.
3
State Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's position and proof
They permit it. Their proof: fils are prices only by convention; the contracting parties can revoke that convention and treat them as specific commodities, so the exchange is valid.
The 'طلب صورته' (seeking the form) argument.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the permissibility view, specific fils can be exchanged at unequal numbers; under the prohibition, any such exchange is riba.
This affects transactions involving copper coins that are not standard currency.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The matn declares 'جاز', so the mufta bihi is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
Imam Muhammad's view is a minority within the school.
