Commentary
This passage is a commentary on rulings regarding riba (usury) in exchanges of certain foodstuffs. It begins by presenting the matn: grapes for raisins, wet wheat for dry, etc. The commentator explains the proof for selling wet dates for dry dates: if the wet dates are actually dates, it is permitted by the hadith 'dates for dates'; if not, by the hadith 'if types differ, sell as you wish.' Inequality due to moisture is considered negligible. Then it discusses the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding grapes and raisins. Abu Hanifa permits if equal in measure (considering them one genus); the two prohibit regardless. The commentator links this to the earlier discussion on wet and dry dates. For barley, Muhammad prohibits because he considers equality at the time of contract essential, while Abu Yusuf makes an exception for wet and dry dates due to a hadith. A distinction is made: if barley is just wetted without swelling, it is permissible. Finally, the term 'al-munqa' (soaked fruit) is defined lexically. Throughout, the Hanafi school's attention to textual proof and rational analogy (qiyas) is evident.

Key Terms
ربا (ribā): Usury or interest in sale transactions, specifically prohibited in exchanges of certain commodities.
جنس (jins): Genus or species of commodity; classifying items into genera determines riba rules.
كيل (kayl): Measurement by volume; used to ensure equality in permissible exchanges.

B) Because they are considered one genus.
C) Because the hadith allows any exchange of food.
D) Because of a rational analogy with wheat.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's dispute on grapes and raisins turns on whether moisture prevents fair equality; the relied-upon view permits equal exchanges.

Exchanging Meats of Different Animals: Same Genus or Different?
Inter-madhhab dispute on genus classification of meats for riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on exchanging meat of different animals and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Meats from different animals are different genera in riba because they have different origins, allowing unequal exchange.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: are all meats considered one genus for riba? The Hanafi school permits unequal exchange of meats from different animals, while a Shafi'i view prohibits it. The dispute hinges on whether shared purpose (nourishment) or specific origin determines genus.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that meats from different animals are different genera, so exchanging them with inequality is permissible.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i (one view) says all meats are one genus due to shared purpose, thus unequal exchange is not allowed.
Al-Muzani's view within Shafi'i school aligns with Hanafi.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Meat is a branch (far') of different origins (usul); difference in origin necessitates difference in genus. The hadith 'If the types differ, sell as you wish' applies.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Unity in nourishment is a general meaning (ma'na 'amm) like taste in edibles, but the specific meaning (ma'na khass) determines genus. Specific differences affect people differently.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi view, one can exchange high-quality beef for low-quality lamb with disparity; under the Shafi'i view, it would be riba and not permissible.

Source Text

And meat of an animal for meat of another animal with inequality. The evidence in all that is that the sale of a genus for a genus without difference in quality is permissible, if equal, and likewise with difference in quality, because of his saying: 'its good and its bad are the same'; it was not permissible for sale of genus for genus in any way, because of his saying: 'if the two types differ, then sell as you wish.' (Meat of an animal for meat of another animal with inequality). (1) His saying: 'meat of an animal... etc'. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible, because the purpose of meat is nourishment and strength, and differences in purpose beyond that go back to description. And we say: Meat is a branch of different origins; difference in origin necessarily causes difference in the branch, and unity in nourishment and consideration of the general meaning is like taste in edibles, but the considered thing is unity in the specific meaning. So said in 'al-Nihaya'. And he said in 'Kamal al-Diraya' (2): from al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) that the two meats and milks are one genus, because of the unity of purpose - nourishment and strength. And his apparent madhhab, which is the choice of al-Muzani, is that meats are different genera like our madhhab. Likewise, the more correct of his madhhab regarding milks is that they are different genera, because their origins are of different genera, such that they are not combined with each other in zakat, and they have different names by attribution, like wheat flour and barley flour, different in purpose, for some people desire some meats and milks over others, and some benefit them and some harm them. And Malik said: Meats are three genera: birds, domesticated and wild animals, and sea creatures. And by this said Ahmad (may Allah be pleased with him) in one narration. And he restricted the animal to being from a different genus, because if it were from the same genus, like beef for beef, then it is not permissible? (The text cuts off). (1) Al-Zayla'i said in Nasb al-Raya (4:37) and Ibn Hajar in al-Diraya (2:156): We did not find it in this wording, and it is taken from the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (may Allah be pleased with him), who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, hand to hand; whoever increases or asks for increase has committed riba, the giver and receiver are alike in it.' In Muslim (3:1211) and others. (2) (Kamal al-Diraya, folio 412).
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on whether meats of different animals are considered one genus for riba purposes. The matn states that exchanging meat of one animal for meat of another with inequality is permissible. The commentator explains the general evidence: selling a genus for a genus, whether similar or different in quality, is permissible if equal; differing types can be exchanged in any amount. Then the specific ruling on meat is discussed, followed by the objection of Imam al-Shafi'i, who considers all meats as one genus because of shared purpose (nourishment). The Hanafi response is that meat is a branch of different origins (different animals), so they are different genera. The commentator also notes that the more authoritative view of al-Shafi'i's school (according to al-Muzani) is that meats are different genera, aligning with the Hanafi view. Imam Malik's classification into three genera is also mentioned. The discussion highlights the Hanafi emphasis on specificity of cause ('illa) rather than generic purpose.

Key Terms
لحم (lahm): Meat of an animal; here, considered as a commodity subject to riba rules.
جنس (jins): Genus; in riba, determining whether items are same or different genus affects permissibility of unequal exchange.
متفاضلاً (mutafādilan): With disparity or inequality in quantity or quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Shafi'i view (one opinion) that all meats are one genus?
A) The hadith explicitly says so.
B) The purpose of meat is nourishment and strength.
C) All animals are from the same species.
D) The Companions agreed on this ruling.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines genus by origin rather than purpose, so meats from different animals are different genera, permitting unequal exchange.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ruling on Selling Meat of Different Animals with Disparity
Commentary on permissibility of exchanging meats of different species

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on exchanging meat with disparity and explain why meats from different animals are considered different genera, using the principle of specific purpose over general purpose.

Core Idea
Meats differ by origin, not just purpose — disparity allowed across genera.

When can you trade 1 kg of beef for 2 kg of mutton? The Hanafi school says yes, because beef and mutton belong to different legal genera. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya defends that view against the Shafi'i objection, unpacking the criteria for determining genus in riba transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
State the Hanafi position on exchanging meat of different animals with disparity (tafadul) and the Shafi'i objection.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Locate the hadith principle cited: 'When the types differ, sell as you wish,' and the reasoning from origins.
The hadith is abstracted from the riba hadith.
3
Understand the concept of jins
Analyze how Hanafis define genus: origin (asl), name (ism), form (surah), and purpose (maqsad). Note the emphasis on specific meaning over general meaning.
4
Trace the dispute resolution
See how the Hanafi response rebuts the Shafi'i purpose argument by asserting that meat is a branch of different origins, so different genera necessarily result.
Also note that al-Muzani (Shafi'i) agreed with Hanafis.
5
Apply the principle to other cases
Understand the extensions to milk, vinegar, fat, and bread, and the exception for bird meat.
Bird meat is not customarily weighed or measured.

And (the ruling on) meat of one animal with meat of another with disparity. And the evidence in all that is that if selling one genus for another without difference of quality is permissible even if equal, and likewise with difference of quality, because of his saying: 'Its good and its bad are the same', selling one genus for another was not permissible in any manner, because of his saying: 'When the types differ, sell as you wish'. (Meat of one animal with meat of another with disparity) (1) His saying: 'Meat of one animal... etc.': Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible because the purpose of meat is nutrition and strength, and differences in purposes thereafter return to description. And we say: Meat is a branch of different origins; difference in origin necessitates difference of the branch necessarily, and unity in nutrition and consideration of the general meaning like taste in foods, and what is considered is unity in the specific meaning. Thus in al-Nihayah. And it is said in Kamal al-Dirayah from al-Shafi'i: That meats and milks are one genus due to unity of purpose, which is nutrition and strength, but the apparent of his madhhab – and it is the choice of al-Muzani – is that meats are different genera like our madhhab. And likewise the more correct of his madhhab regarding milks is that they are different genera because their origins are of different genera, to the extent that some are not combined with others in zakat, and their names differ by attribution, like wheat flour with barley flour, and their purposes differ, for some people desire some meats and milks over others, and some benefit them while others harm them. And Malik said: Meats are three genera: birds, domesticated and wild animals, and aquatic animals, and Ahmad agreed in one narration. And the animal is restricted to being from another genus because if it were from the same genus – like beef with... about it. In Muslim (3:1211) and others. (2) Kamal al-Diraya (folio 412).

And likewise milk, and likewise vinegar of inferior dates with vinegar of grapes, and belly fat with tail fat or with meat, and bread with wheat or with flour, or with sawiq, even if one of them is on credit, and according to this is given fatwa. (Regarding) buffalo, and cow's milk with buffalo milk: it is not permissible to sell one for the other with disparity because they are one genus; and for this reason their milks are combined with one another in zakat. And likewise meat of goats and sheep, and meat of Arabian camels and Bactrian camels, and their milk. Unlike hair of goats and wool of sheep, for they are two genera due to difference of form and purpose. If it is said: This is problematic regarding selling meat of birds with disparity among themselves, for it is permissible, and it is one genus. It is answered: That is because it is not usually weighed or measured, unlike milks and meats of other than birds, for they are weighed. Thus in al-Mabsut. End summarized. [1] His saying: 'And likewise milk': i.e., just as it is permissible to sell meat of one animal with meat of another with disparity, likewise it is permissible to sell milk of one animal with milk of another with disparity. [2] His saying: 'And likewise... etc.': And likewise it is permissible to sell each of vinegar of inferior dates and vinegar of grapes with the other because the difference between their origins is established, and similarly between their branches. And they specifically mentioned vinegar of inferior dates – even though the ruling of vinegar of every date with grape vinegar is the same – because they used to make vinegar mostly from inferior dates, so the speech came according to custom. It is said in Muntaha al-Arab: 'Daqal' (with vowel movement): a type of date that is not specifically named and is not one of the well-known types. End. (3) His saying: 'And belly fat... etc.': i.e., it is permissible to sell them with disparity, even if all are from sheep, because they are different genera due to difference of names, forms, and purposes. As for difference of names, it is apparent because meat is not called fat, nor fat called meat. As for difference of forms, because the form is what occurs in the mind when one imagines it, and... (1) Al-Daqal: a type of bad dates. See al-Tulba (p.109). (2) Al-Sawiq: what is made from wheat and barley. See al-Misbah (p.296) and Taj al-Arus (25:480) and others.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on the ruling of selling meat of one animal for meat of another with disparity (tafadul). The author begins by stating the ruling: it is permissible, and provides the general evidence from hadith: when two items are of different types (genus), you may sell as you wish, with or without equality. The key principle is that meat from different animals constitutes different genera (ajnas) due to different origins, even though the general purpose (nutrition) is the same. The passage then presents the inter-madhhab dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i initially held that all meats are one genus because the overarching purpose is nutrition and strength, so exchange with disparity is not allowed. However, the Hanafi response is that meat is a branch (far') of different origins (usul); difference in origin necessarily makes the branch different. The specific purpose (ma'na khass) is considered, not just the general purpose. The Hanafi position is further supported by noting that even within al-Shafi'i's school, al-Muzani (a prominent Shafi'i) agreed with the Hanafi view that meats are different genera. The passage also mentions Malik's division of meats into three genera and Ahmad's similar view. The commentary then extends the ruling to milk, vinegar, fat, and bread, all with the same reasoning: when the origins differ or the names and forms differ, the items are considered different genera, allowing disparity. For example, belly fat and tail fat from the same animal are different genera because their names, forms, and purposes differ. The passage addresses an objection regarding bird meat: although bird meat is one genus, it is not customarily weighed or measured, so the riba rules do not apply in the same way. The overall conclusion is that any two food items that differ in genus (jins) due to different origins, names, forms, or purposes can be exchanged with disparity, and this is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): In this passage, jins refers to a legal category of goods for riba purposes, determined by origin (asl), name (ism), form (surah), and purpose (maqsad).
متفاضلاً (mutafādilan): Exchanging goods with disparity in quantity or weight (e.g., more of one for less of another).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, why is it permissible to sell beef with mutton with disparity (e.g., 1 kg beef for 2 kg mutton)?
A) Because both are meat and share the same general purpose of nutrition.
B) Because they are from different origins (cow vs. sheep), making them different genera.
C) Because both are weighed and measured in the same way.
D) Because the hadith explicitly allows disparity for all types of meat.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, meats from different animals are different genera because the origin (asl) differs, overriding the shared general purpose of nutrition; thus exchange with disparity is permissible.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Selling Disparate Items: The Hanafi Ruling on Ribawi Items of Different Species
Ruling with proof on disparity in ribawi items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling items of different species with disparity and apply the criteria of genus (jins) to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
Disparity is allowed between different species; similarity of genus triggers riba restrictions.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary clarifies the rule that selling ribawi items with disparity (mutafādilan) is permissible only if they belong to different genera (ajnās). It examines borderline cases like milk, vinegar, fat, meat, and bread, and addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding bread and wheat. Understanding the concept of jins is critical for avoiding riba in such transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Read the matn statement: items like milk from different animals, vinegar from different sources, fat and meat, bread with wheat/flour can be sold with disparity. Note the general principle: if the items are the same genus (jins wāhid), disparity is not allowed; if different, it is allowed.
The rule applies to ribawi items that are customarily weighed or measured.
2
Understand the criterion of jins
The commentary explains that jins is determined by three factors: name (ism), form (sūrah), and purpose (maqsūd). For example, cow and buffalo milk are one genus because they share the name 'milk' and same purpose, even from different animals. In contrast, goat hair and sheep wool are different genera due to different name and purpose.
The Hanafi definition of jins for riba includes items that are customarily weighed or measured and share the same essential characteristics.
3
Analyze exceptional cases
Consider the objection about bird meat: all bird meat is one species but it is permissible to sell with disparity. The answer is that bird meat is not customarily weighed or measured, so the effective cause of riba (weight/measure) is absent. This shows that the prohibition is tied to the customary handling of the item.
Items that are not customarily weighed/measured fall outside the scope of riba prohibition.
4
Examine the bread dispute
For bread with wheat/flour on credit (nasī'ah), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad disallow it due to the presence of flour in bread causing ambiguity of genus; Abu Yusuf allows it because bread becomes countable/weighable and thus different genus from wheat/flour. The fatwa is given on Abu Yusuf's view due to necessity.
Also note that salam (advance sale) of bread is valid according to Abu Yusuf if weight and type are specified, but invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad due to variation in bread quality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب الربا وكذا اللبن، وكذا خل الدِّقْل بخل العنب، وشحم البطن بالإلية أو باللحم، والخبز بالبر أو الدقيق، أو بالسويق وإن كان أحدهما نسيئة، وبه يُفْتَى وكذا اللبن، وكذا " خل الدقل بخل العنب، وشحم البطن بالإلية أو باللحم، والخبز بالبر أو الدقيق ، أو بالسويق ، وإن كان أحدهما نسيئة، وبه يُفْتَى) الجاموس، ولبن البقر بلبن الجاموس لم يجز بيعُ أحدهما بالآخر متفاضلاً ؛ لأنهما جنس واحد ؛ ولهذا يضم لبنهما أحدهما إلى الآخرِ في الزَّكاة، وكذا لحم المعز والضأن ولحم العراب والبخت، ولبنهما بخلافِ شعرِ المعز وصوفِ الغنم ؛ فإنّهما جنسان؛ لاختلاف الصورة والمقصود.
فإن قيل : يشكل على هذا بيعُ لحم الطّير بعضُهُ ببعض متفاضلاً، فإنَّه يجوز، وهو جنس واحد. أجيب : بأن ذلك باعتبار أنه لا يوزنُ عادة ولا يكالُ بخلاف الألبانِ ولحمانِ غيرِ الطير، فإنّها توزن كذا في «المبسوط». انتهى باختصار. [١]قوله : وكذا اللبن ؛ أي كما جاز بيع لحم حيوان بلحم حيوان آخر متفاضلاً، كذلك جاز بيع لبن حيوان بلبن حيوان آخر متفاضلا. [٢] قوله : وكذا... الخ ؛ وكذا جازَ بيع كلُّ واحدٍ من خل الدقْلِ والعنب بالآخر ؛ لأن الاختلاف بين أصليهما ثابت، فكذا بين ثانيهما ، وإنما خصوا حَلَّ الدَّقلِ بالذكرِ مع أنَّ الحكم في خل كلِّ تمر مع خل العنب واحد ؛ لأنهم كانوا يجعلونَ الخل من الدَّقْلِ غالباً، فالكلام خرج على مخرج العادة ، قال في منتهى الأرب: دقل: محركة : خرماي که او را اسمي بخصوص و از انواع مشهورة بناشد. انتهى.
(۳) قوله : وشحم البطن...الخ ؛ أي ويجوز بيعها متفاضلاً، وإن كانت كلها من الضأن ؛ لأنها أجناس مختلفة ؛ لاختلافِ الأسماء والصور والمقاصد، أما اختلاف الأسماء فظاهر ؛ لأنه لا يطلقُ اللّحم على الشحم، ولا الشحم على اللحم. وأما اختلاف الصور ؛ فلأنَّ الصورة ما يحصلُ منه في الذهن عند تصورِه ، ولا شك في ذلك عند تصور هذه الأشياء.
وأما اختلاف المقاصد، فلكل واحدٍ منهما من الخواص ما لا يوجد في غيره كما لا يخفى على من طالع كتب الطب، وإن شئت التفصيل فارجع إليها.
[١] قوله : لأن الخبز صارَ عددياً ؛ كما عند محمد ، أو موزوناً كما عند أبي يوسف الله ، فخرج من أن يكون مكيلاً من كل وجه، والبرّ كيلي بالنص، وكذا الدقيق ولم يجمعها القدر من كل وجه، فلم توجد علة الربا.
وعن أبي حنيفة له أنه لا يجوز ، وهو قول الشافعي وأحمد له ؛ لأنَّ في الخبز أجزاء الدقيق، وذلك يورث شبهة المجانسة ، والفتوى على الجواز، وهذا إذا كانـا نقدين : أي حكم الجواز إذا لم يكن أحد البدلين الذين هما الخبز والبر، أو الخبز والدقيق نسيئة، وإن كان الخبز نسيئة والبر والدقيق نقداً، أو كان البر أو الدقيق نسيئة والخبر نقداً.
فعلى الثاني جازَ أيضاً ؛ لأنه أسلم موزوناً في مكيل، يمكن ضبط صفتِهِ ومعرفة مقداره ، وعلى الأول يجوز عند أبي يوسف الله إذا ذكر وزناً معلوماً ونوعاً معلوماً، وبه يفتى ؛ لحاجة الناس إليه، لكن ينبغي أن يحتاط وقت القبض، حتى يقبض من الجنس الذي سمّى ؛ لئلا يصير مستبدلاً بالمسلم فيه قبل القبض.
وذكر ابن رستم له في «نوادره»: أنَّ على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد ه لا يصح السلم في الخبز لا وزناً ولا عدداً ؛ لأنه يتفاوت بالعجن ، والنضج، ويكون منه الثقيلُ والخفيف ؛ ولهذه العلة أفسد أبو حنيفة الله استقراضه ؛ لأنَّ السلم أوسع بابـاً مـن القرض، حتى جازَ السلم في الثياب ، ولم يجز القرض فيها، كذا في «كمال الدراية».
The book of sales, chapter on riba. And similarly milk, and similarly vinegar of inferior dates with vinegar of grapes, and abdominal fat with tail fat or with meat, and bread with wheat or flour or with sawiq, even if one of them is on credit, and according to this fatwa is given. And similarly milk, and similarly vinegar of inferior dates with vinegar of grapes, and abdominal fat with tail fat or with meat, and bread with wheat or flour or with sawiq, even if one of them is on credit, and according to this fatwa is given. Buffalo and cow's milk with buffalo's milk: it is not permissible to sell one with the other with disparity because both are the same species; hence the milk of the two is added together in zakat. Similarly goat's meat and sheep's meat, and Arab camel's meat and Bactrian camel's meat, and their milk, unlike goat's hair and sheep's wool, for these are two different species due to difference in form and purpose. If it is said: This is problematic with the sale of bird meat one part for another with disparity, for it is permissible and it is one species. The answer is that this is because it is not customarily weighed or measured, unlike milk and meats of non-birds, for these are weighed. Thus in Al-Mabsut. Ended with abbreviation. [1] His statement: 'And similarly milk' meaning just as it is permissible to sell the meat of one animal with the meat of another with disparity, similarly it is permissible to sell the milk of one animal with the milk of another with disparity. [2] His statement: 'And similarly...' etc.; similarly it is permissible to sell each of vinegar of inferior dates and vinegar of grapes with the other because the difference between their two origins is established, so likewise between their two derivatives. They specifically mentioned vinegar of inferior dates even though the ruling for vinegar of any dates with vinegar of grapes is the same because they usually made vinegar from inferior dates, so the speech follows custom. He said in Muntaha al-Arab: 'Daqal: shakl: a date that has no specific name and is not among the famous types.' End. (3) His statement: 'And abdominal fat...' etc.; i.e., it is permissible to sell them with disparity, even if they are all from sheep, because they are different species due to difference of names, forms, and purposes. As for the difference of names, it is apparent because meat is not called fat, nor fat called meat. As for the difference of forms, because the form is what is obtained in the mind when conceptualizing it, and there is no doubt about that when conceptualizing these things. As for the difference of purposes, each has properties not found in the other, as is not hidden from one who has read medical books; if you want detail, refer to them. [1] His statement: 'Because bread became countable' according to Muhammad, or weighable according to Abu Yusuf, so it is no longer measurable in every respect, and wheat is measurable by text, and similarly flour, and the measure does not unite them in every respect, so the effective cause of riba is not present. From Abu Hanifa that it is not permissible, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, because in bread there are parts of flour, and that creates an ambiguity of conspecificity, but the fatwa is on permissibility. This is when both are spot: i.e., the ruling of permissibility when neither of the two substitutes, which are bread and wheat, or bread and flour, is on credit. If the bread is on credit and the wheat or flour is spot, or the wheat or flour is on credit and the bread is spot, then according to the second it is also permissible because it is a weighable item deposited into a measurable item whose description can be controlled and quantity known. According to the first, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf if a known weight and known type are mentioned, and according to this fatwa is given due to people's need, but one should be cautious at the time of receipt until he receives the same genus he specified, lest he become substituted for the salam goods before receipt. Ibn Rustom mentioned in his Nawadir that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, salam in bread is not valid, whether by weight or by count, because it varies with kneading and ripeness, and some is heavy and some light; for this reason Abu Hanifa invalidated its loan, because salam is broader in scope than loan, even salam in clothes is permissible but loan in them is not, as in Kamal al-Diraya.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from the matn regarding the permissibility of selling certain items with disparity or on credit. The author explains that milk from different animals, vinegar from different origins, fat and meat, and bread with wheat or flour can be sold with disparity because they are different species (ajnās). The key criteria is whether the items are the same genus (jins): if they are the same genus, like cow and buffalo milk, they cannot be sold with disparity due to riba; if different, it is allowed. The passage also addresses an objection about bird meat, clarifying that bird meat is not weighed or measured, so it is treated differently. The commentary then delves into each item: milk, vinegar, fat/meat, and bread. For bread, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider bread countable, Abu Yusuf considers it weighable, and this affects the ruling on selling bread with wheat on credit. Abu Yusuf allows it, and the fatwa is given accordingly. Additionally, salam (advance sale) of bread is discussed, with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad deeming it invalid due to variation in bread quality, while Abu Yusuf allows it. The passage emphasizes that the effective cause of riba (the combination of genus and measure) is absent when items change category (from measure to weight/count).

Key Terms
متفاضلاً (mutafādilan): Selling one item for another of the same type but with an unequal quantity (disparity).
نسيئة (nasī'ah): Deferred payment or delivery; selling on credit.
جنس (jins): Genus or species; used here to determine whether items are of the same category for riba purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it NOT permissible to sell cow milk with buffalo milk with disparity?
A) Because cow and buffalo are different animals, so their milk should be different genera.
B) Because both are milk and considered the same genus; disparity would involve riba.
C) Because milk is not a ribawi item.
D) Because the Prophet (s) explicitly forbade it.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of selling ribawi items with disparity depends on whether they are the same genus; if different, disparity is allowed; if same, it is prohibited unless the items are not customarily weighed or measured.

Exchanging Good for Bad in Ribawi Items: Equal Quantity Required
Ruling with proof on equal exchange of ribawi items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging good and bad quality ribawi items of the same genus and identify the hadith that prohibits disparity.

Core Idea
Quality does not justify disparity in ribawi exchanges—equal quantity is required.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary clarifies a fundamental principle of riba al-fadl: when exchanging two items of the same ribawi genus, any excess in quantity is prohibited, regardless of quality differences. The commentator cites a hadith that explicitly equates good and bad quality in such transactions. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage rules on selling good quality for bad quality of ribawi items. The ruling is that it is not permissible (haram) if any disparity in quantity exists.
Ribawi items are those weighed or measured and consumable.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'جيدها ورديئها سواء' (Its good and its bad are equal). This is an ahad hadith.
The hadith is reported in multiple collections.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The word 'سواء' (equal) indicates that the two quantities must be the same. Quality does not affect the ruling; only quantity matters. Any excess is riba.
4
Note the Example
The commentator gives an example: selling unripe dates (busr) for ripe dates (tamr) with disparity is also prohibited. This illustrates that the same principle applies even when the quality differs markedly.
The example is specific to dates, a ribawi item.
5
Understand the Cross-Madhhab Agreement
All schools of thought agree on this prohibition for same-genus ribawi items, though there are minor exceptions for certain non-food items.
The Hanafi position is based on the clear hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢]قوله : لا يجوز بيع الجيد بالرديء من الربوي ؛ أي مما فيه الربا، ولا يجوز بيع البسر بالتمر متفاضلاً، أما الأول فلقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «جيدها ورديئها سواء» وهذا في
[2] His statement: 'Prohibition of selling good quality for bad quality from ribawi items'; meaning from what involves riba, and it is not permissible to sell unripe dates for ripe dates with disparity. As for the first, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Its good and its bad are equal'. And this is in
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement 'No selling of good for bad among ribawi items'. The commentator explains that this includes all ribawi items, and gives the example of selling unripe dates (busr) for ripe dates (tamr) with disparity. The proof is the hadith 'Its good and its bad are equal', meaning that when exchanging the same species, equality in quantity is required regardless of quality. The commentary is incomplete here, but the principle is clear: quality difference does not justify disparity in ribawi transactions; the exchange must be equal in measure or weight.

Key Terms
جيد (jayyid): High quality; the better variety of a ribawi item.
رديء (radī'): Low quality; the inferior variety of a ribawi item.
ربوي (ribawī): An item subject to riba rules (usually those that are weighable or measurable and consumable).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on selling high-quality rice for a larger quantity of low-quality rice?
A) Permissible because the quality difference justifies the disparity.
B) Permissible because rice is not a ribawi item.
C) Prohibited because all rice is the same genus and must be exchanged equally.
D) Prohibited only if wheat is involved.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'جيدها ورديئها سواء' establishes that when exchanging same-genus ribawi items, equality in quantity is required regardless of quality differences.

The General Prohibition of Selling Good for Bad in Ribawi Items
Main ruling with hadith proof and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule prohibiting quality-differentiated exchange of ribawi items and identify its proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Quality difference does not justify inequality in ribawi exchange; the good and bad are equal by law.

When you buy a staple food or precious metal, the law does not allow paying more for a better version if the type is the same. This lesson unpacks the hadith-based ruling that forbids selling good quality for bad quality of the same ribawi item, and introduces key exceptions like bread.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage opens with 'لا بيع الجيد بالرديء من الربوي' – this is the starting point. Recognize that this is a prohibition (tahrim).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith 'جيدها ورديئها سواء' as the proof. Understand that this hadith is a general statement applying to all ribawi items.
The hadith is from the chapter of riba.
3
Apply the ruling to examples
The passage then gives examples: busr for tamr, wheat for flour, etc. Trace how each example falls under the general rule – because they are the same genus.
Busr and tamr are both dates; wheat and flour are both wheat.
4
Note the exception for bread
Bread is singled out as an exception; the passage says 'وإنما يجوز الخبز بالبر' – bread may be sold for wheat. This hints at an important intra-madhhab dispute.
We will cover this dispute in detail in the next lesson.

Source Text

(۱) البسر : التمر قبل أن إرطابه لخضاضته ، وذلك إذا لون ولم ينضج، وإذا نضج فقد أرطب. ينظر: (تاج العروس(١٠ : ١٧٤)، وغيره.
The sale of good (quality) for bad (quality) of ribawi (items) is not permitted. And bread may be sold for wheat, because bread has become countable; this is when both are cash (spot). If the bread is on credit, and the wheat or flour is cash, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, and this is the fatwa. (The statement) 'The sale of good for bad of ribawi' is doubted upon visualizing these things. [2] As for the difference in objectives, each of them has properties not found in the other, as is not hidden from one who studies medical books; if you want detail, refer to them. [1] His saying: 'Because bread has become countable' as with Muhammad, or weighable as with Abu Yusuf, so it has come out of being measurable from every aspect, and wheat is measurable by text, and likewise flour, and the quantity does not combine them from every aspect, so the cause of riba is not found. From Abu Hanifa that it is not permissible, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, because bread contains parts of flour, and that gives a semblance of homogeneity, and the fatwa is on permissibility. This is when both are cash: that is, the ruling of permissibility when neither of the two countervalues (bread and wheat, or bread and flour) is on credit. If the bread is on credit and the wheat or flour is cash, or the wheat or flour is on credit and the bread is cash, then according to the second (case) it is also permissible, because it is a salam of a weighable item for a measurable item where its description can be specified and its quantity known. According to the first (case), it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf if a known weight and known type are mentioned, and this is the fatwa due to people's need for it, but one should be careful at the time of receipt to receive from the type mentioned, lest it become an exchange for the salaf before receipt. Ibn Rustom mentioned in his 'Nawadir' that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, salam in bread is not valid whether by weight or count, because it varies with kneading and maturity, and some is heavy and some light; for this reason Abu Hanifa invalidated its loan because salam is broader in scope than loan, so salam in clothes is permitted while loan in them is not, as in 'Kamal al-Dirayah'. [2] His saying: 'It is not permissible to sell good for bad of ribawi' meaning from what contains riba, and it is not permissible to sell unripe dates for dried dates with excess. As for the first, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Their good and their bad are equal.' This is in the Book of Sales, Chapter of Riba. [Page 223] And unripe dates for dried dates only equally, and wheat for flour or saweeq, or flour for saweeq with excess or equally, and olives for oil, and sesame for vinegar until the oil and vinegar are more than what is in the olives and sesame, and unripe dates for dried dates only equally, and wheat for flour or saweeq, or flour for saweeq with excess or equally, and olives for oil, and sesame for vinegar until the oil and vinegar are more than what is in the olives and sesame of the ribawi wealth; and for this reason the author (may Allah have mercy on him) specified saying 'of the ribawi'. As for the second (the case of unripe dates for dried dates), because the term 'tamr' applies to 'busr' so they are of the same type, and excess is not permissible in homogeneous types; thus sale in these two forms is only permissible equally. In 'Muntaha al-Arab': 'Busr' (with damma) is unripe dates, and the sin may be damma, and its stages... (Persian description of date ripeness stages) ... and after that tamr. End. [1] His saying: 'And wheat...' meaning it is not permissible to sell wheat for flour (i.e., its flour) or for saweeq (i.e., its saweeq) with excess or equally. As for with excess, because each of flour and saweeq is wheat from one aspect even if they have a specific name, because each consists of parts of wheat, for grinding only separates parts, and the whole does not become another species by separation. As for equally, because the standard is measurement by volume, which is not uniform between them and wheat due to compaction in them and looseness in wheat. According to Malik and Ahmad (in one narration) it is permissible to sell wheat for flour and for saweeq both by volume and weight. And it is not permissible to sell flour for saweeq with excess or equally, according to Abu Hanifa, due to the persistence of homogeneity from one aspect, since saweeq is parts of roasted wheat and flour is parts of unroasted wheat, and selling roasted wheat for unroasted wheat is not valid in any case, so likewise selling flour for saweeq.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on the ruling that ribawi items of the same type cannot be exchanged with a difference in quality. The passage begins by stating the general rule: 'لا بيع الجيد بالرديء من الربوي' — the good quality may not be sold for bad in ribawi items. It then provides an exception: bread (khubz) may be sold for wheat (burr) because bread has become countable (or weighable, according to Abu Yusuf) and thus no longer falls under the same ribawi category as wheat by measure. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that it is not permissible because bread still contains flour parts, giving a semblance of homogeneity; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it, and the fatwa is on permissibility. The passage then details the conditions for this permissibility, including whether the exchange is spot or on credit. It discusses salam (advance sale) in bread, citing Ibn Rustom's Nawadir that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, salam in bread is invalid due to variation in weight. The commentary then returns to the main ruling, citing the hadith 'جيدها ورديئها سواء' (good and bad are equal) as proof. It lists specific prohibited exchanges: busr (unripe dates) for tamr (dried dates) unless equal, wheat for flour or saweeq, olives for oil, sesame for vinegar (unless output exceeds input), and explains the reasoning. A lengthy Persian definition of busr stages is included from Muntaha al-Arab. Finally, it discusses the sale of wheat for flour or saweeq, noting that flour and saweeq are considered the same genus as wheat, so excess is not allowed, though Malik and Ahmad allow it. The sale of flour for saweeq is prohibited because they are essentially roasted and unroasted wheat, which are of the same genus.

Key Terms
الربوي (al-ribawi): Items that are subject to riba (usury) rules – generally gold, silver, and staple foodstuffs sold by weight or measure.
الخبز (al-khubz): Bread, considered in the context of riba; it is processed from wheat/flour.
البسر (al-busr): Unripe dates, before they reach the stage of tamr (ripe dried dates).
السلم (al-salam): An advance sale where payment is made upfront for goods to be delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the lesson, what is the ruling on exchanging 1 kg of high-quality wheat for 2 kg of low-quality wheat?
A) Permissible because of quality difference.
B) Permissible if both parties agree.
C) Prohibited.
D) Permissible only if the seller does not intend riba.

Key Takeaway
The general rule: ribawi items of the same type must be exchanged equal in quantity regardless of quality; the hadith 'جيدها ورديئها سواء' is the primary proof.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

The Sale of Bread for Wheat: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Riba
Intra-Hanafi dispute with conditions for permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on selling bread for wheat, and state the mufta bihi (operative) ruling with its conditions.

Core Idea
Bread is not fully ribawi because processing changes its nature; the fatwa allows its sale for wheat with inequality.

This lesson dives into a celebrated intra-Hanafi dispute: can you sell a loaf of bread for a cup of wheat? The answer hinges on whether bread remains a ribawi item. We will examine the proofs, the conditions for permissibility, and why the fatwa favors Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is whether bread (khubz) can be sold for wheat (burr) or flour (daqiq) with inequality, i.e., one loaf for two cups of wheat.
2
State the opposing views
Abu Hanifa (and Shafi'i, Ahmad) say it is not permissible. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is permissible under conditions. Note the reasons given.
Abu Hanifa: semblance of homogeneity (shubhat al-mujanasah). Sahibayn: bread becomes countable/weighable, no longer fully kali.
3
Analyse the Sahibayn's proof
They argue that bread is not purely measure-based (kayli); it is processed and sold by weight or count. Thus the cause of riba (jins wa kayl) is incomplete.
4
Identify the conditions for permissibility
The passage specifies: both items must be spot (nagd). If one is credit, then it is a salam transaction, with additional conditions like specifying weight and type.
The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf's view on credit case.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text says 'وبه يفتى' (with this is the fatwa) indicating the permissive view of Abu Yusuf is relied upon for practical application.

(۱) البسر : التمر قبل أن إرطابه لخضاضته ، وذلك إذا لون ولم ينضج، وإذا نضج فقد أرطب. ينظر: (تاج العروس(١٠ : ١٧٤)، وغيره.
The sale of good (quality) for bad (quality) of ribawi (items) is not permitted. And bread may be sold for wheat, because bread has become countable; this is when both are cash (spot). If the bread is on credit, and the wheat or flour is cash, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf, and this is the fatwa. (The statement) 'The sale of good for bad of ribawi' is doubted upon visualizing these things. [2] As for the difference in objectives, each of them has properties not found in the other, as is not hidden from one who studies medical books; if you want detail, refer to them. [1] His saying: 'Because bread has become countable' as with Muhammad, or weighable as with Abu Yusuf, so it has come out of being measurable from every aspect, and wheat is measurable by text, and likewise flour, and the quantity does not combine them from every aspect, so the cause of riba is not found. From Abu Hanifa that it is not permissible, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, because bread contains parts of flour, and that gives a semblance of homogeneity, and the fatwa is on permissibility. This is when both are cash: that is, the ruling of permissibility when neither of the two countervalues (bread and wheat, or bread and flour) is on credit. If the bread is on credit and the wheat or flour is cash, or the wheat or flour is on credit and the bread is cash, then according to the second (case) it is also permissible, because it is a salam of a weighable item for a measurable item where its description can be specified and its quantity known. According to the first (case), it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf if a known weight and known type are mentioned, and this is the fatwa due to people's need for it, but one should be careful at the time of receipt to receive from the type mentioned, lest it become an exchange for the salaf before receipt. Ibn Rustom mentioned in his 'Nawadir' that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, salam in bread is not valid whether by weight or count, because it varies with kneading and maturity, and some is heavy and some light; for this reason Abu Hanifa invalidated its loan because salam is broader in scope than loan, so salam in clothes is permitted while loan in them is not, as in 'Kamal al-Dirayah'. [2] His saying: 'It is not permissible to sell good for bad of ribawi' meaning from what contains riba, and it is not permissible to sell unripe dates for dried dates with excess. As for the first, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Their good and their bad are equal.' This is in the Book of Sales, Chapter of Riba. [Page 223] And unripe dates for dried dates only equally, and wheat for flour or saweeq, or flour for saweeq with excess or equally, and olives for oil, and sesame for vinegar until the oil and vinegar are more than what is in the olives and sesame, and unripe dates for dried dates only equally, and wheat for flour or saweeq, or flour for saweeq with excess or equally, and olives for oil, and sesame for vinegar until the oil and vinegar are more than what is in the olives and sesame of the ribawi wealth; and for this reason the author (may Allah have mercy on him) specified saying 'of the ribawi'. As for the second (the case of unripe dates for dried dates), because the term 'tamr' applies to 'busr' so they are of the same type, and excess is not permissible in homogeneous types; thus sale in these two forms is only permissible equally. In 'Muntaha al-Arab': 'Busr' (with damma) is unripe dates, and the sin may be damma, and its stages... (Persian description of date ripeness stages) ... and after that tamr. End. [1] His saying: 'And wheat...' meaning it is not permissible to sell wheat for flour (i.e., its flour) or for saweeq (i.e., its saweeq) with excess or equally. As for with excess, because each of flour and saweeq is wheat from one aspect even if they have a specific name, because each consists of parts of wheat, for grinding only separates parts, and the whole does not become another species by separation. As for equally, because the standard is measurement by volume, which is not uniform between them and wheat due to compaction in them and looseness in wheat. According to Malik and Ahmad (in one narration) it is permissible to sell wheat for flour and for saweeq both by volume and weight. And it is not permissible to sell flour for saweeq with excess or equally, according to Abu Hanifa, due to the persistence of homogeneity from one aspect, since saweeq is parts of roasted wheat and flour is parts of unroasted wheat, and selling roasted wheat for unroasted wheat is not valid in any case, so likewise selling flour for saweeq.

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on the ruling that ribawi items of the same type cannot be exchanged with a difference in quality. The passage begins by stating the general rule: 'لا بيع الجيد بالرديء من الربوي' — the good quality may not be sold for bad in ribawi items. Exchange of Unripe Dates (Busr) for Ripe Dates (Tamr)
Ruling on busr-tamr exchange with genus rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on exchanging busr for tamr and explain why they are considered the same genus in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Busr and tamr are the same genus; exchange must be equal to avoid riba.

This passage clarifies that unripe dates (busr) and ripe dates (tamr) belong to the same genus for riba purposes. The author provides a detailed definition of date ripening stages and states that sale between them is valid only if equal in measure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on busr and tamr
Find the phrase 'والبسر بالتمر إلا متساوياً'. Note that the author permits exchange only if equal.
The matn simply says 'except equal'.
2
Understand the genus reasoning
The author explains that 'tamr' applies to busr, so they are homogeneous; excess is prohibited.
This is based on the principle of riba al-fadl.
3
Read the definition of busr stages
The passage from Muntaha al-Arab lists the stages of date development from pollinated flower to ripe date.
This is a lexicographical detail; the key point is that busr is included under 'tamr' in legal sense.

والبسر بالتمر إلا متساوياً ، والبُرِّ بالدقيق أو بالسويق، أو الدقيق بالسويق متفاضلاً أو متساوياً، والزّيتون بالزيت، والسمسم بالخل حتى يكونَ الزَّيتُ والخل أكثر مما في الزيتون والسمسم والبسر) بالتمر إلا متساوياً ، والبُرِّ بالدقيق أو بالسويق، أو الدقيق بالسويق متفاضلاً أو متساوياً، والزيتون بالزيت، والسمسم بالخل حتى يكونَ الزَّيَتُ والخل أكثر مما في الزيتون والسمسم الأموال الربوية ؛ ولهذا قيد المصنف الله لقوله : من الربوي، وأما الثاني : فلإطلاق التمر على البسر فيكون من جنسه ، والتَّفاضلُ لا يجوز في المتجانسين ، فلا يجوزُ البيع في هاتين الصورتين إلا متساوياً. قال في منتهى الأرب: بسر : بالضم غوره خرما، ويضم السين، وانجداز شکوفه رخر ما اول طاهر شود انر اطلع خوانند وجون بسته گردد سیاب گویند و هرگاه سبنردگرد گردد جدال وجون اندکي کلان گردد آنر ابغو خوانند وجون ازان کلان شود بسرست و بعد ازان مخطم بعد ازان موکت بعد از ان بذنوب بعد از ان جمسه بعد ازان خالع وجون يحتكي آن بانتهار سدر طب نامند و بعد ازان تمر. انتهى. [١] قوله : والبر...الخ ؛ يعني لا يجوز بيع البر بالدقيق : أي بدقيق البر أو بالسويق ، أي بسويق البر متفاضلاً أو متساوياً. أما متفاضلاً ؛ فلان كل واحدٍ من الدقيق والسويق بر من وجه وإن اختص باسم ؛ لأن كل واحد منهما من أجزاء البُرِّ ، فإنَّ الطحن لا يوجد إلا تفريق الأجزاء، والمجتمع لا يصير بالتفريق جنساً آخر. وأما متساوية ؛ فلان المعيار فيه الكيل، وهو غير مستو بينهما وبين البر؛ لاكتنازهما فيه، وتخلخل البر. ويجوز عند مالك وأحمد الله في رواية بيع البر بالدقيق وبالسويق كيلاً ووزناً. ولا يجوز بيع الدقيق بالسويق متفاضلاً أو متساوياً، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له ؛ لبقاء المجانسة من وجه، إذ السويقُ أجزاء حنطة مقلية، والدقيق أجزاء حنطة غير مقلية، وبيع الحنطة المقليَّةِ بغيرِ المقلية لا يصح بحال، فكذا بيع الدقيق بالسويق. (۱) البسر : التمر قبل أن إرطابه لخضاضته ، وذلك إذا لون ولم ينضج، وإذا نضج فقد أرطب. ينظر: (تاج العروس(١٠ : ١٧٤)، وغيره. ويستقرضُ الخبز وزناً لا عدداً عند أبي يوسف له وبه يُفْتَى (١ ليكون بعضُ الزَّيتِ بالزيت الذي في الزيتون ، والباقي بالنَّجير" [۲] ( ويستقرض الخبز وزناً لا عدداً عند أبي يوسف له، وبه يُفْتَى) ، أما عند أبي حنيفة له لا يجوز لا وزناً ولا عدداً وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد الله : يجوز بيع الدقيق بالسويق كيف ما كان؛ لأنهما جنسان مختلفان ؛ لاختلاف اسمهما والمقصود منهما ؛ لأنَّ أحدهما يصلح لما لا يصلح الآخر، فإنَّ الدقيق مثلاً يصلح للخبز، والسويق لا يصلح له، بل يلت بالسمن أو العسل ويؤكل، والدقيق ليس كذلك. وأجيب : بأن التغذي معظم المقصود، وهو يشملها، ولا يضـر فـواتُ بعض المقاصدِ كالحنطة المقلية مع غير المقلية، فإنَّ المقلية لا يصلح للزراعة مثلاً، وغير المقلية تصلح لها، وذا لا يوجب اختلاف الجنس، فكذا الدقيق مع السويق، كذا في «كمال الدراية وغيره من الكتب المبسوطة. (١) قوله : ليكون ...الخ ؛ واعلم أنَّ بيع الزيتون بالزيت على أربعة أوجه : . إن علم أن الزيت الذي في الزيتون أكثر من الزيت المنفصل ، لم يصح لتحققِ الفضل الخالي عن العوض من حيث زيادة الدهن والتفل. . وكذا إن علم أنه مثله ؛ لأنَّ التفل يكون فضلاً خالياً عن العوض. . وإن علم أن الزيت المنفصل أكثر جازَ والفضلُ بالتفل، وهذه الثلاثة بالإجماع. ٤. وإن لم يعلم أنه مثله ، أو أكثر منه، أو أقلّ منه صح عند زفره ؛ لأنَّ الجواز هو الأصل، والفساد لوجودِ الفضل الخالي عن العوض، فما لم يعلم لا يفسد البيع، وعندنا : لا يصح؛ لأنَّ الفضل الذي هو متوهّم الوجودِ كالمتحقق في بـاب الـربا احتياطاً ، كذا في «كمال الدراية»(۲) نقلا عن شرح «الوافي». [٢] قوله : بالثجير؛ تجير كامير کنجاره که تفل باشد كذا في منتهى الأرب»، وكنجاره بمعنی کنجارا ست که نخاله کنجد و هر تخم که روغن آنرا کشیده باشند ، كذا في «البرهان القاطع».
And unripe dates with ripe dates except equal, and wheat with flour or with sawiq, or flour with sawiq (whether) excess or equal, and olives with oil, and sesame with vinegar such that the oil and vinegar are more than what is in the olives and sesame. ... (Unripe dates with ripe dates except equal). The author conditioned by his saying 'from the ribawi'. And the second: because the term 'tamr' applies to busr, so it is of its genus, and excess is not allowed among homogeneous items. So sale in these two forms is not allowed except equally. He said in Muntaha al-Arab: Busr: with damma of ba, it is raw dates ... end. [1] His statement: 'And wheat...' meaning: It is not permissible to sell wheat for flour, i.e., wheat flour, or for sawiq, i.e., wheat sawiq, whether excess or equal. As for excess: because each of flour and sawiq is wheat in a sense, even if it has a specific name; because each of them is from parts of the wheat grain, for grinding only separates parts, and the aggregate does not become another genus by separation. And as for equal: because the standard is by measure, and it is not equal between them and wheat due to their density in it and the loosening of wheat. It is permissible according to Malik and Ahmad in one narration to sell wheat for flour and sawiq by measure and weight. And selling flour for sawiq is not permissible, whether excess or equal, according to Abu Hanifa; due to genus remaining similar in some respect, for sawiq is parts of parched wheat, and flour is parts of unparched wheat, and selling parched wheat for unparched is not valid at all, so too selling flour for sawiq. (1) Busr: dates before they become ripe due to freshness, when they color but do not ripen; when they ripen they become rutab. See Taj al-Arus (10:174) etc. And bread is borrowed by weight, not by count, according to Abu Yusuf, and with it is given fatwa. [1] So that some of the oil (is exchanged) for the oil in the olives, and the remainder for the marc. [2] (And bread is borrowed by weight, not by count, according to Abu Yusuf, and with it is given fatwa). As for Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible neither by weight nor by count. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Selling flour for sawiq is permissible in any way because they are different genera; due to difference in their names and the intended purpose; because one is suitable for what the other is not, for flour is suitable for bread, and sawiq is not suitable for it, rather it is mixed with ghee or honey and eaten, and flour is not like that. And it was answered: that nutrition is the main purpose, and it includes them, and the loss of some purposes does not matter, like parched wheat with unparchd, for parched is not suitable for cultivation, etc., and the other is suitable for it, and that does not necessitate difference in genus, so too flour with sawiq, as in Kamal al-Dirayah and other detailed books. (1) His statement: 'so that...' Know that selling olives for oil has four aspects: 1. If it is known that the oil in the olives is more than the separate oil, it is not valid due to the existence of excess without compensation in terms of increase of oil and pulp. 2. Similarly if it is known that it is equal, because the pulp is excess without compensation. 3. If it is known that the separate oil is more, it is valid, and the excess is for the pulp; these three are by consensus. 4. If it is not known whether it is equal, or more, or less, it is valid according to Zufar because permissibility is the original, and invalidity is due to existence of excess without compensation, and as long as it is not known, the sale is not invalidated. According to us: it is not valid because the excess which is possibly existing is like actual in the chapter of riba as a precaution, as in Kamal al-Dirayah quoting from Sharh al-Wafi. [2] His statement: 'with marc': Tajir like amir, is the marc, as in Muntaha al-Arab, and 'kunjara' means the husk of sesame and any seed whose oil has been extracted, as in al-Burhan al-Qati.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rulings on ribawi transactions, specifically dealing with the exchange of similar food items. The author, commenting on the matn of Al-Wiqayah, begins with the case of unripe dates (busr) for ripe dates (tamr): they are of the same genus, so exchange must be equal in measure. He then defines 'busr' in detail from Muntaha al-Arab, showing the stages of date development. Next, he addresses wheat (burr) exchanged for flour (daqiq) or parched grain (sawiq). The Hanafi position holds that these are all from the same genus despite name changes, so excess is prohibited. He notes that Malik and Ahmad allow such exchange. For flour with sawiq, Abu Hanifa forbids it, analogizing to parched versus unparched wheat, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider them different genera and allow it. The author then discusses olives with oil: if the oil in the olives is equal or more, sale is invalid due to ambiguous excess; if the separate oil is known to be more, it is valid; if unknown, Zufar allows but the Hanafis do not, as precaution against riba. Finally, the ruling on borrowing bread: Abu Yusuf says it is permissible by weight (not count), and this is the fatwa; Abu Hanifa forbids it entirely. The commentary maintains the Hanafi framework, presenting the relied-upon positions.

Key Terms
بسر (busr): Unripe dates, before the stage of rutab.
تمر (tamr): Ripe dates, the final stage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why must busr and tamr be exchanged equally?
A) Because they are both fruits
B) Because they are considered the same genus (jins)
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically forbade unequal exchange of dates
D) Because busr is cheaper than tamr

Key Takeaway
Busr and tamr belong to the same genus, so their exchange must be equal in measure to avoid riba.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Exchange of Wheat (Burr) for Flour (Daqiq) or Parched Grain (Sawiq)
Ruling on wheat with its derivatives: prohibited even if equal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging wheat for its processed forms and explain the reasoning based on genus identity.

Core Idea
Flour and sawiq are still wheat in essence; excess exchange is riba.

This section addresses whether wheat can be exchanged for its derivatives—flour and parched grain. The Hanafi school holds that they remain the same genus, so any excess is prohibited. The author also mentions that Malik and Ahmad allow such exchange by weight or volume.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on burr with daqiq or sawiq
Find the statement 'لا يجوز بيع البر بالدقيق أو بالسويق متفاضلاً أو متساوياً'.
Both excess and equal are prohibited at face value; but equal is also prohibited? Actually the text says 'متفاضلاً أو متساوياً' meaning both are prohibited. This is interesting because equal exchange would normally be permissible. Here it's prohibited because the measure (kayl) is not equal due to density differences.
2
Understand the reasoning for excess
Flour and sawiq are from parts of wheat; grinding does not change the genus.
The author analogizes to parched vs. unparched wheat.
3
Understand the reasoning for equal exchange
Even if equal in weight, the measure (kayl) differs because flour and sawiq are denser than wheat grain.
The standard for ribawi items is measure (kayl), not weight, according to the Hanafi school.
4
Note the opposing view
Malik and Ahmad allow selling wheat for flour or sawiq by weight or volume.
They consider them different genera or allow by weight.

والبسر بالتمر إلا متساوياً ، والبُرِّ بالدقيق أو بالسويق، أو الدقيق بالسويق متفاضلاً أو متساوياً، والزّيتون بالزيت، والسمسم بالخل حتى يكونَ الزَّيتُ والخل أكثر مما في الزيتون والسمسم والبسر) بالتمر إلا متساوياً ، والبُرِّ بالدقيق أو بالسويق، أو الدقيق بالسويق متفاضلاً أو متساوياً، والزيتون بالزيت، والسمسم بالخل حتى يكونَ الزَّيَتُ والخل أكثر مما في الزيتون والسمسم الأموال الربوية ؛ ولهذا قيد المصنف الله لقوله : من الربوي، وأما الثاني : فلإطلاق التمر على البسر فيكون من جنسه ، والتَّفاضلُ لا يجوز في المتجانسين ، فلا يجوزُ البيع في هاتين الصورتين إلا متساوياً. قال في منتهى الأرب: بسر : بالضم غوره خرما، ويضم السين، وانجداز شکوفه رخر ما اول طاهر شود انر اطلع خوانند وجون بسته گردد سیاب گویند و هرگاه سبنردگرد گردد جدال وجون اندکي کلان گردد آنر ابغو خوانند وجون ازان کلان شود بسرست و بعد ازان مخطم بعد ازان موکت بعد از ان بذنوب بعد از ان جمسه بعد ازان خالع وجون يحتكي آن بانتهار سدر طب نامند و بعد ازان تمر. انتهى. (١) قوله : ليكون ...الخ ؛ واعلم أنَّ بيع الزيتون بالزيت على أربعة أوجه : . إن علم أن الزيت الذي في الزيتون أكثر من الزيت المنفصل ، لم يصح لتحققِ الفضل الخالي عن العوض من حيث زيادة الدهن والتفل. . وكذا إن علم أنه مثله ؛ لأنَّ التفل يكون فضلاً خالياً عن العوض. . وإن علم أن الزيت المنفصل أكثر جازَ والفضلُ بالتفل، وهذه الثلاثة بالإجماع. ٤. وإن لم يعلم أنه مثله ، أو أكثر منه، أو أقلّ منه صح عند زفره ؛ لأنَّ الجواز هو الأصل، والفساد لوجودِ الفضل الخالي عن العوض، فما لم يعلم لا يفسد البيع، وعندنا : لا يصح؛ لأنَّ الفضل الذي هو متوهّم الوجودِ كالمتحقق في بـاب الـربا احتياطاً ، كذا في «كمال الدراية»(۲) نقلا عن شرح «الوافي». And unripe dates with ripe dates except equal, and wheat with flour or with sawiq, or flour with sawiq (whether) excess or equal, and olives with oil, and sesame with vinegar such that the oil and vinegar are more than what is in the olives and sesame. ... (Unripe dates with ripe dates except equal). The author conditioned by his saying 'from the ribawi'. And the second: because the term 'tamr' applies to busr, so it is of its genus, and excess is not allowed among homogeneous items. So sale in these two forms is not allowed except equally. He said in Muntaha al-Arab: Busr: with damma of ba, it is raw dates ... end. [1] His statement: 'And wheat...' meaning: It is not permissible to sell wheat for flour, i.e., wheat flour, or for sawiq, i.e., wheat sawiq, whether excess or equal. As for excess: because each of flour and sawiq is wheat in a sense, even if it has a specific name; because each of them is from parts of the wheat grain, for grinding only separates parts, and the aggregate does not become another genus by separation. And as for equal: because the standard is by measure, and it is not equal between them and wheat due to their density in it and the loosening of wheat. It is permissible according to Malik and Ahmad in one narration to sell wheat for flour and sawiq by measure and weight. And selling flour for sawiq is not permissible, whether excess or equal, according to Abu Hanifa; due to genus remaining similar in some respect, for sawiq is parts of parched wheat, and flour is parts of unparched wheat, and selling parched wheat for unparched is not valid at all, so too selling flour for sawiq. (1) Busr: dates before they become ripe due to freshness, when they color but do not ripen; when they ripen they become rutab. See Taj al-Arus (10:174) etc. And bread is borrowed by weight, not by count, according to Abu Yusuf, and with it is given fatwa. [1] So that some of the oil (is exchanged) for the oil in the olives, and the remainder for the marc. [2] (And bread is borrowed by weight, not by count, according to Abu Yusuf, and with it is given fatwa). As for Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible neither by weight nor by count. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Selling flour for sawiq is permissible in any way because they are different genera; due to difference in their names and the intended purpose; because one is suitable for what the other is not, for flour is suitable for bread, and sawiq is not suitable for it, rather it is mixed with ghee or honey and eaten, and flour is not like that. And it was answered: that nutrition is the main purpose, and it includes them, and the loss of some purposes does not matter, like parched wheat with unparchd, for parched is not suitable for cultivation, etc., and the other is suitable for it, and that does not necessitate difference in genus, so too flour with sawiq, as in Kamal al-Dirayah and other detailed books. (1) His statement: 'so that...' Know that selling olives for oil has four aspects: 1. If it is known that the oil in the olives is more than the separate oil, it is not valid due to the existence of excess without compensation in terms of increase of oil and pulp. 2. Similarly if it is known that it is equal, because the pulp is excess without compensation. 3. If it is known that the separate oil is more, it is valid, and the excess is for the pulp; these three are by consensus. 4. If it is not known whether it is equal, or more, or less, it is valid according to Zufar because permissibility is the original, and invalidity is due to existence of excess without compensation, and as long as it is not known, the sale is not invalidated. According to us: it is not valid because the excess which is possibly existing is like actual in the chapter of riba as a precaution, as in Kamal al-Dirayah quoting from Sharh al-Wafi. [2] His statement: 'with marc': Tajir like amir, is the marc, as in Muntaha al-Arab, and 'kunjara' means the husk of sesame and any seed whose oil has been extracted, as in al-Burhan al-Qati.

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the rulings on ribawi transactions, specifically dealing with the exchange of similar food items. The author, commenting on the matn of Al-Wiqayah, begins with the case of unripe dates (busr) for ripe dates (tamr): they are of the same genus, so exchange must be equal in measure. He then defines 'busr' in detail from Muntaha al-Arab, showing the stages of date development. Next, he addresses wheat (burr) exchanged for flour (daqiq) or parched grain (sawiq). The Hanafi position holds that these are all from the same genus despite name changes, so excess is prohibited. He notes that Malik and Ahmad allow such exchange. For flour with sawiq, Abu Hanifa forbids it, analogizing to parched versus unparched wheat, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider them different genera and allow it. The author then discusses olives with oil: if the oil in the olives is equal or more, sale is invalid due to ambiguous excess; if the separate oil is known to be more, it is valid; if unknown, Zufar allows but the Hanafis do not, as precaution against riba. Finally, the ruling on borrowing bread: Abu Yusuf says it is permissible by weight (not count), and this is the fatwa; Abu Hanifa forbids it entirely. The commentary maintains the Hanafi framework, presenting the relied-upon positions.

Key Terms
بر (burr): Wheat grain.
دقيق (daqīq): Flour, ground from wheat.
سويق (sawīq): Parched grain (often wheat) ground or whole.
كيل (kayl): Measure of volume, the standard for ribawi foodstuffs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is selling wheat for flour prohibited even if equal in weight?
A) Because flour is a different genus
B) Because the measure (kayl) is not equal due to density
C) Because wheat is superior to flour
D) Because the Prophet forbade it specifically

Key Takeaway
Wheat and its products (flour, sawiq) are the same genus; exchange is prohibited unless equal in measure, which is practically impossible, hence prohibited entirely.
